2483 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Greet was the feeste in Atthenes that day,</B><BR>
2484 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek the lusty seson of that May</B><BR>
2485 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Made every wight to been in swich plesaunce</B><BR>
2486 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That al that Monday justen they and daunce,</B><BR>
2487 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And spenden it in Venus heigh servyse.</B><BR>
2488 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But by the cause that they sholde ryse</B><BR>
2489 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Eerly, for to seen the grete fight,</B><BR>
2490 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Unto hir reste wenten they at nyght.</B><BR>
2491 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And on the morwe, whan that day gan sprynge,</B><BR>
2492 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of hors and harneys noyse and claterynge</B><BR>
2493 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther was in hostelryes al aboute,</B><BR>
2494 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And to the paleys rood ther many a route</B><BR>
2495 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of lordes upon steedes and palfreys.</B><BR>
2496 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther maystow seen devisynge of harneys</B><BR>
2497 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So unkouth and so riche, and wroght so weel</B><BR>
2498 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of goldsmythrye, of browdynge, and of steel;</B><BR>
2499 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The sheeldes brighte, testeres, and trappures,</B><BR>
2500 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Gold-hewen helmes, coats of mail, cote-armures;</B><BR>
2501 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lordes in parementz on hir courseres,</B><BR>
2502 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Knyghtes of retenue, and eek squieres</B><BR>
2503 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Nailynge the speres, and helmes bokelynge;</B><BR>
2504 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Giggynge of sheeldes, with layneres lacynge --</B><BR>
2505 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>There as nede is they weren no thyng ydel;</B><BR>
2506 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The fomy steedes on the golden brydel</B><BR>
2507 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Gnawynge, and faste the armurers also</B><BR>
2508 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With fyle and hamer prikynge to and fro;</B><BR>
2509 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yemen on foote, and communes many oon</B><BR>
2510 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With shorte staves, thikke as they may goon;</B><BR>
2511 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Pypes, trompes, nakers, clariounes,</B><BR>
2512 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That in the bataille blowen blody sounes;</B><BR>
2513 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The paleys ful of peple up and doun,</B><BR>
2514 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Heere thre, ther ten, holdynge hir questioun,</B><BR>
2515 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Dyvynynge of thise Thebane knyghtes two.</B><BR>
2516 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Somme seyden thus, somme seyde "it shal be so";</B><BR>
2517 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Somme helden with hym with the blake berd,</B><BR>
2518 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Somme with the balled, somme with the thikke herd;</B><BR>
2519 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Somme seyde he looked grymme, and he wolde fighte:</B><BR>
2520 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"He hath a sparth of twenty pound of wighte."</B><BR>
2521 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thus was the halle ful of divynynge,</B><BR>
2522 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Longe after that the sonne gan to sprynge.</B><BR>
2523 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The grete Theseus, that of his sleep awaked</B><BR>
2524 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With mynstralcie and noyse that was maked,</B><BR>
2525 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Heeld yet the chambre of his paleys riche</B><BR>
2526 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Til that the Thebane knyghtes, bothe yliche</B><BR>
2527 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Honured, were into the paleys fet.</B><BR>
2528 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Duc Theseus was at a wyndow set,</B><BR>
2529 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Arrayed right as he were a god in trone.</B><BR>
2530 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The peple preesseth thiderward ful soone</B><BR>
2531 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hym for to seen, and doon heigh reverence,</B><BR>
2532 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek to herkne his heste and his sentence.</B><BR>
2533 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>An heraud on a scaffold made an "Oo!"</B><BR>
2534 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Til al the noyse of peple was ydo,</B><BR>
2535 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And whan he saugh the peple of noyse al stille,</B><BR>
2536 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Tho shewed he the myghty dukes wille:</B><BR>
2537 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"The lord hath of his heigh discrecioun</B><BR>
2538 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Considered that it were destruccioun</B><BR>
2539 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To gentil blood to fighten in the gyse</B><BR>
2540 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of mortal bataille now in this emprise.</B><BR>
2541 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wherfore, to shapen that they shal nat dye,</B><BR>
2542 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He wol his firste purpos modifye.</B><BR>
2543 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>No man therfore, up peyne of los of lyf,</B><BR>
2544 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>No maner shot, ne polax, ne short knyf</B><BR>
2545 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Into the lystes sende or thider brynge;</B><BR>
2546 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne short swerd, for to stoke with poynt bitynge,</B><BR>
2547 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>No man ne drawe, ne bere it by his syde.</B><BR>
2548 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne no man shal unto his felawe ryde</B><BR>
2549 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But o cours with a sharpe ygrounde spere;</B><BR>
2550 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Foyne, if hym list, on foote, hymself to were.</B><BR>
2551 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And he that is at meschief shal be take</B><BR>
2552 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And noght slayn, but be broght unto the stake</B><BR>
2553 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That shal ben ordeyned on either syde;</B><BR>
2554 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But thider he shal by force, and there abyde.</B><BR>
2555 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And if so falle the chieftayn be take</B><BR>
2556 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>On outher syde, or elles sleen his make,</B><BR>
2557 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>No lenger shal the turneiynge laste.</B><BR>
2558 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>God spede you! Gooth forth and ley on faste!</B><BR>
2559 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With long swerd and with mace fighteth youre fille.</B><BR>
2560 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Gooth now youre wey; this is the lordes wille."</B><BR>
2561 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The voys of peple touchede the hevene,</B><BR>
2562 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So loude cride they with murie stevene,</B><BR>
2563 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"God save swich a lord, that is so good</B><BR>
2564 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He wilneth no destruccion of blood!"</B><BR>
2565 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Up goon the trompes and the melodye,</B><BR>
2566 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And to the lystes rit the compaignye,</B><BR>
2567 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>By ordinance, thurghout the citee large,</B><BR>
2568 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hanged with clooth of gold, and nat with sarge.</B><BR>
2569 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful lik a lord this noble duc gan ryde,</B><BR>
2570 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thise two Thebans upon either syde,</B><BR>
2571 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And after rood the queene and Emelye,</B><BR>
2572 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And after that another compaignye</B><BR>
2573 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of oon and oother, after hir degree.</B><BR>
2574 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thus they passen thurghout the citee,</B><BR>
2575 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And to the lystes come they by tyme.</B><BR>
2576 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>It nas nat of the day yet fully pryme</B><BR>
2577 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan set was Theseus ful riche and hye,</B><BR>
2578 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ypolita the queene, and Emelye,</B><BR>
2579 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And othere ladys in degrees aboute.</B><BR>
2580 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Unto the seetes preesseth al the route.</B><BR>
2581 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And westward, thurgh the gates under Marte,</B><BR>
2582 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Arcite, and eek the hondred of his parte,</B><BR>
2583 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With baner reed is entred right anon;</B><BR>
2584 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in that selve moment Palamon</B><BR>
2585 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Is under Venus, estward in the place,</B><BR>
2586 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With baner whyt and hardy chiere and face.</B><BR>
2587 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In al the world, to seken up and doun,</B><BR>
2588 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So evene, withouten variacioun,</B><BR>
2589 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther nere swiche compaignyes tweye,</B><BR>
2590 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For ther was noon so wys that koude seye</B><BR>
2591 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That any hadde of oother avauntage</B><BR>
2592 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of worthynesse, ne of estaat, ne age,</B><BR>
2593 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So evene were they chosen, for to gesse.</B><BR>
2594 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in two renges faire they hem dresse.</B><BR>
2595 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan that hir names rad were everichon,</B><BR>
2596 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That in hir nombre gyle were ther noon,</B><BR>
2597 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Tho were the gates shet, and cried was loude:</B><BR>
2598 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Do now youre devoir, yonge knyghtes proude!"</B><BR>
2599 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The heraudes lefte hir prikyng up and doun;</B><BR>
2600 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now ryngen trompes loude and clarioun.</B><BR>
2601 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther is namoore to seyn, but west and est</B><BR>
2602 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In goon the speres ful sadly in arrest;</B><BR>
2603 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In gooth the sharpe spore into the syde.</B><BR>
2604 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther seen men who kan juste and who kan ryde;</B><BR>
2605 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther shyveren shaftes upon sheeldes thikke;</B><BR>
2606 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He feeleth thurgh the herte-spoon the prikke.</B><BR>
2607 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Up spryngen speres twenty foot on highte;</B><BR>
2608 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Out goon the swerdes as the silver brighte;</B><BR>
2609 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The helmes they tohewen and toshrede;</B><BR>
2610 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Out brest the blood with stierne stremes rede;</B><BR>
2611 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With myghty maces the bones they tobreste.</B><BR>
2612 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He thurgh the thikkeste of the throng gan threste;</B><BR>
2613 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther stomblen steedes stronge, and doun gooth al,</B><BR>
2614 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He rolleth under foot as dooth a bal;</B><BR>
2615 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He foyneth on his feet with his tronchoun,</B><BR>
2616 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And he hym hurtleth with his hors adoun;</B><BR>
2617 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He thurgh the body is hurt and sithen ytake,</B><BR>
2618 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Maugree his heed, and broght unto the stake;</B><BR>
2619 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As forward was, right there he moste abyde.</B><BR>
2620 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Another lad is on that oother syde.</B><BR>
2621 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And some tyme dooth hem Theseus to reste,</B><BR>
2622 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hem to refresshe and drynken, if hem leste.</B><BR>
2623 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful ofte a day han thise Thebanes two</B><BR>
2624 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Togydre ymet, and wroght his felawe wo;</B><BR>
2625 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Unhorsed hath ech oother of hem tweye.</B><BR>
2626 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther nas no tygre in the vale of Galgopheye,</B><BR>
2627 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan that hir whelp is stole whan it is lite,</B><BR>
2628 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So crueel on the hunte as is Arcite</B><BR>
2629 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For jelous herte upon this Palamon.</B><BR>
2630 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne in Belmarye ther nys so fel leon,</B><BR>
2631 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That hunted is, or for his hunger wood,</B><BR>
2632 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne of his praye desireth so the blood,</B><BR>
2633 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As Palamon to sleen his foo Arcite.</B><BR>
2634 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The jelous strokes on hir helmes byte;</B><BR>
2635 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Out renneth blood on bothe hir sydes rede.</B><BR>
2636 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Som tyme an ende ther is of every dede.</B><BR>
2637 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For er the sonne unto the reste wente,</B><BR>
2638 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The stronge kyng Emetreus gan hente</B><BR>
2639 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This Palamon, as he faught with Arcite,</B><BR>
2640 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And made his swerd depe in his flessh to byte,</B><BR>
2641 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And by the force of twenty is he take</B><BR>
2642 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Unyolden, and ydrawen to the stake.</B><BR>
2643 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in the rescus of this Palamoun</B><BR>
2644 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The stronge kyng Lygurge is born adoun,</B><BR>
2645 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And kyng Emetreus, for al his strengthe,</B><BR>
2646 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Is born out of his sadel a swerdes lengthe,</B><BR>
2647 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So hitte him Palamoun er he were take.</B><BR>
2648 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But al for noght; he was broght to the stake.</B><BR>
2649 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His hardy herte myghte hym helpe naught:</B><BR>
2650 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He moste abyde, whan that he was caught,</B><BR>
2651 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>By force and eek by composicioun.</B><BR>
2652 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Who sorweth now but woful Palamoun,</B><BR>
2653 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That moot namoore goon agayn to fighte?</B><BR>
2654 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And whan that Theseus hadde seyn this sighte,</B><BR>
2655 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Unto the folk that foghten thus echon</B><BR>
2656 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He cryde, "Hoo! namoore, for it is doon!</B><BR>
2657 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I wol be trewe juge, and no partie.</B><BR>
2658 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Arcite of Thebes shal have Emelie,</B><BR>
2659 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That by his fortune hath hire faire ywonne."</B><BR>
2660 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Anon ther is a noyse of peple bigonne</B><BR>
2661 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For joye of this, so loude and heighe withalle</B><BR>
2662 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>It semed that the lystes sholde falle.</B><BR>
2663 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>What kan now faire Venus doon above?</B><BR>
2664 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>What seith she now? What dooth this queene of love,</B><BR>
2665 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But wepeth so, for wantynge of hir wille,</B><BR>
2666 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Til that hir teeres in the lystes fille?</B><BR>
2667 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>She seyde, "I am ashamed, doutelees."</B><BR>
2668 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Saturnus seyde, "Doghter, hoold thy pees!</B><BR>
2669 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Mars hath his wille, his knyght hath al his boone,</B><BR>
2670 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And, by myn heed, thow shalt been esed soone."</B><BR>
2671 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The trompours, with the loude mynstralcie,</B><BR>
2672 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The heraudes, that ful loude yelle and crie,</B><BR>
2673 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Been in hire wele for joye of daun Arcite.</B><BR>
2674 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But herkneth me, and stynteth noyse a lite,</B><BR>
2675 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Which a myracle ther bifel anon.</B><BR>
2676 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This fierse Arcite hath of his helm ydon,</B><BR>
2677 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And on a courser, for to shewe his face,</B><BR>
2678 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He priketh endelong the large place</B><BR>
2679 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lokynge upward upon this Emelye;</B><BR>
2680 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And she agayn hym caste a freendlich ye</B><BR>
2681 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>(For wommen, as to speken in comune,</B><BR>
2682 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thei folwen alle the favour of Fortune)</B><BR>
2683 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And was al his chiere, as in his herte.</B><BR>
2684 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Out of the ground a furie infernal sterte,</B><BR>
2685 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>From Pluto sent at requeste of Saturne,</B><BR>
2686 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For which his hors for fere gan to turne,</B><BR>
2687 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And leep aside, and foundred as he leep;</B><BR>
2688 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And er that Arcite may taken keep,</B><BR>
2689 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He pighte hym on the pomel of his heed,</B><BR>
2690 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That in the place he lay as he were deed,</B><BR>
2691 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His brest tobrosten with his sadel-bowe.</B><BR>
2692 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As blak he lay as any cole or crowe,</B><BR>
2693 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So was the blood yronnen in his face.</B><BR>
2694 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Anon he was yborn out of the place,</B><BR>
2695 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With herte soor, to Theseus paleys.</B><BR>
2696 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Tho was he korven out of his harneys</B><BR>
2697 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in a bed ybrought ful faire and blyve,</B><BR>
2698 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For he was yet in memorie and alyve,</B><BR>
2699 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And alwey criynge after Emelye.</B><BR>
2700 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Duc Theseus, with al his compaignye,</B><BR>
2701 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Is comen hoom to Atthenes his citee,</B><BR>
2702 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With alle blisse and greet solempnitee.</B><BR>
2703 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al be it that this aventure was falle,</B><BR>
2704 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He nolde noght disconforten hem alle.</B><BR>
2705 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Men seyde eek that Arcite shal nat dye;</B><BR>
2706 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He shal been heeled of his maladye.</B><BR>
2707 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And of another thyng they weren as fayn,</B><BR>
2708 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That of hem alle was ther noon yslayn,</B><BR>
2709 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al were they soore yhurt, and namely oon,</B><BR>
2710 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That with a spere was thirled his brest boon.</B><BR>
2711 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To othere woundes and to broken armes</B><BR>
2712 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Somme hadden salves, and somme hadden charmes;</B><BR>
2713 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Fermacies of herbes, and eek save</B><BR>
2714 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>They dronken, for they wolde hir lymes have.</B><BR>
2715 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For which this noble duc, as he wel kan,</B><BR>
2716 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Conforteth and honoureth every man,</B><BR>
2717 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And made revel al the longe nyght</B><BR>
2718 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Unto the straunge lordes, as was right.</B><BR>
2719 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne ther was holden no disconfitynge</B><BR>
2720 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But as a justes or a tourneiynge;</B><BR>
2721 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For soothly ther was no disconfiture.</B><BR>
2722 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For fallyng nys nat but an aventure,</B><BR>
2723 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne to be lad by force unto the stake</B><BR>
2724 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Unyolden, and with twenty knyghtes take,</B><BR>
2725 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>O persone allone, withouten mo,</B><BR>
2726 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And haryed forth by arme, foot, and too,</B><BR>
2727 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eke his steede dryven forth with staves</B><BR>
2728 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With footmen, bothe yemen and eek knaves --</B><BR>
2729 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>It nas arretted hym no vileynye;</B><BR>
2730 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther may no man clepen it cowardye.</B><BR>
2731 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For which anon duc Theseus leet crye,</B><BR>
2732 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To stynten alle rancour and envye,</B><BR>
2733 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The gree as wel of o syde as of oother,</B><BR>
2734 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eyther syde ylik as ootheres brother;</B><BR>
2735 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And yaf hem yiftes after hir degree,</B><BR>
2736 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And fully heeld a feeste dayes three,</B><BR>
2737 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And conveyed the kynges worthily</B><BR>
2738 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Out of his toun a journee largely.</B><BR>
2739 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And hoom wente every man the righte way.</B><BR>
2740 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther was namoore but "Fare wel, have good day!"</B><BR>
2741 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of this bataille I wol namoore endite,</B><BR>
2742 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But speke of Palamon and of Arcite.</B><BR>
2743 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Swelleth the brest of Arcite, and the soore</B><BR>
2744 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Encreesseth at his herte moore and moore.</B><BR>
2745 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The clothered blood, for any lechecraft,</B><BR>
2746 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Corrupteth, and is in his bouk ylaft,</B><BR>
2747 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That neither veyne-blood, ne ventusynge,</B><BR>
2748 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne drynke of herbes may ben his helpynge.</B><BR>
2749 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The vertu expulsif, or animal,</B><BR>
2750 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Fro thilke vertu cleped natural</B><BR>
2751 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne may the venym voyden ne expelle.</B><BR>
2752 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The pipes of his longes gonne to swelle,</B><BR>
2753 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And every lacerte in his brest adoun</B><BR>
2754 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Is shent with venym and corrupcioun.</B><BR>
2755 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hym gayneth neither, for to gete his lif,</B><BR>
2756 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Vomyt upward, ne dounward laxatif.</B><BR>
2757 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al is tobrosten thilke regioun;</B><BR>
2758 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Nature hath now no dominacioun.</B><BR>
2759 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And certeinly, ther Nature wol nat wirche,</B><BR>
2760 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Fare wel phisik! Go ber the man to chirche!</B><BR>
2761 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This al and som, that Arcita moot dye;</B><BR>
2762 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For which he sendeth after Emelye,</B><BR>
2763 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Palamon, that was his cosyn deere.</B><BR>
2764 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne seyde he thus, as ye shal after heere:</B><BR>
2765 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Naught may the woful spirit in myn herte</B><BR>
2766 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Declare o point of alle my sorwes smerte</B><BR>
2767 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To yow, my lady, that I love moost,</B><BR>
2768 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But I biquethe the servyce of my goost</B><BR>
2769 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To yow aboven every creature,</B><BR>
2770 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Syn that my lyf may no lenger dure.</B><BR>
2771 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Allas, the wo! Allas, the peynes stronge,</B><BR>
2772 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That I for yow have suffred, and so longe!</B><BR>
2773 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Allas, the deeth! Allas, myn Emelye!</B><BR>
2774 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Allas, departynge of oure compaignye!</B><BR>
2775 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Allas, myn hertes queene! Allas, my wyf,</B><BR>
2776 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Myn hertes lady, endere of my lyf!</B><BR>
2777 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>What is this world? What asketh men to have?</B><BR>
2778 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now with his love, now in his colde grave</B><BR>
2779 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Allone, withouten any compaignye.</B><BR>
2780 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Fare wel, my sweete foo, myn Emelye!</B><BR>
2781 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And softe taak me in youre armes tweye,</B><BR>
2782 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For love of God, and herkneth what I seye.</B><BR>
2783 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"I have heer with my cosyn Palamon</B><BR>
2784 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Had strif and rancour many a day agon</B><BR>
2785 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For love of yow, and for my jalousye.</B><BR>
2786 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Juppiter so wys my soule gye,</B><BR>
2787 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To speken of a servaunt proprely,</B><BR>
2788 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With alle circumstances trewely --</B><BR>
2789 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That is to seyen, trouthe, honour, knyghthede,</B><BR>
2790 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wysdom, humblesse, estaat, and heigh kynrede,</B><BR>
2791 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Fredom, and al that longeth to that art --</B><BR>
2792 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So Juppiter have of my soule part,</B><BR>
2793 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As in this world right now ne knowe I non</B><BR>
2794 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So worthy to ben loved as Palamon,</B><BR>
2795 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That serveth yow, and wol doon al his lyf.</B><BR>
2796 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And if that evere ye shul ben a wyf,</B><BR>
2797 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Foryet nat Palamon, the gentil man."</B><BR>
2798 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with that word his speche faille gan,</B><BR>
2799 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For from his feet up to his brest was come</B><BR>
2800 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The coold of deeth, that hadde hym overcome,</B><BR>
2801 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And yet mooreover, for in his armes two</B><BR>
2802 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The vital strengthe is lost and al ago.</B><BR>
2803 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Oonly the intellect, withouten moore,</B><BR>
2804 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That dwelled in his herte syk and soore,</B><BR>
2805 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Gan faillen whan the herte felte deeth.</B><BR>
2806 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Dusked his eyen two, and failled breeth,</B><BR>
2807 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But on his lady yet caste he his ye;</B><BR>
2808 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His laste word was, "Mercy, Emelye!"</B><BR>
2809 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His spirit chaunged hous and wente ther,</B><BR>
2810 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As I cam nevere, I kan nat tellen wher.</B><BR>
2811 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Therfore I stynte; I nam no divinistre;</B><BR>
2812 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of soules fynde I nat in this registre,</B><BR>
2813 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne me ne list thilke opinions to telle</B><BR>
2814 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of hem, though that they writen wher they dwelle.</B><BR>
2815 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Arcite is coold, ther Mars his soule gye!</B><BR>
2816 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now wol I speken forth of Emelye.</B><BR>
2817 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Shrighte Emelye, and howleth Palamon,</B><BR>
2818 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Theseus his suster took anon</B><BR>
2819 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Swownynge, and baar hire fro the corps away.</B><BR>
2820 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>What helpeth it to tarien forth the day</B><BR>
2821 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To tellen how she weep bothe eve and morwe?</B><BR>
2822 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For in swich cas wommen have swich sorwe,</B><BR>
2823 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan that hir housbondes ben from hem ago,</B><BR>
2824 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That for the moore part they sorwen so,</B><BR>
2825 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Or ellis fallen in swich maladye</B><BR>
2826 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That at the laste certeinly they dye.</B><BR>
2827 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Infinite been the sorwes and the teeres</B><BR>
2828 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of olde folk and folk of tendre yeeres</B><BR>
2829 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In al the toun for deeth of this Theban.</B><BR>
2830 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For hym ther wepeth bothe child and man;</B><BR>
2831 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So greet wepyng was ther noon, certayn,</B><BR>
2832 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan Ector was ybroght, al fressh yslayn,</B><BR>
2833 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To Troye. Allas, the pitee that was ther,</B><BR>
2834 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Cracchynge of chekes, rentynge eek of heer.</B><BR>
2835 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Why woldestow be deed," thise wommen crye,</B><BR>
2836 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"And haddest gold ynough, and Emelye?"</B><BR>
2837 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>No man myghte gladen Theseus,</B><BR>
2838 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Savynge his olde fader Egeus,</B><BR>
2839 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That knew this worldes transmutacioun,</B><BR>
2840 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As he hadde seyn it chaunge bothe up and doun,</B><BR>
2841 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Joye after wo, and wo after gladnesse,</B><BR>
2842 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And shewed hem ensamples and liknesse.</B><BR>
2843 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Right as ther dyed nevere man," quod he,</B><BR>
2844 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"That he ne lyvede in erthe in some degree,</B><BR>
2845 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Right so ther lyvede never man," he seyde,</B><BR>
2846 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"In al this world, that som tyme he ne deyde.</B><BR>
2847 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This world nys but a thurghfare ful of wo,</B><BR>
2848 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And we been pilgrymes, passynge to and fro.</B><BR>
2849 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Deeth is an ende of every worldly soore."</B><BR>
2850 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And over al this yet seyde he muchel moore</B><BR>
2851 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To this effect, ful wisely to enhorte</B><BR>
2852 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The peple that they sholde hem reconforte.</B><BR>
2853 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Duc Theseus, with al his bisy cure,</B><BR>
2854 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Caste now wher that the sepulture</B><BR>
2855 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of goode Arcite may best ymaked be,</B><BR>
2856 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek moost honurable in his degree.</B><BR>
2857 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And at the laste he took conclusioun</B><BR>
2858 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That ther as first Arcite and Palamoun</B><BR>
2859 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hadden for love the bataille hem bitwene,</B><BR>
2860 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That in that selve grove, swoote and grene,</B><BR>
2861 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther as he hadde his amorouse desires,</B><BR>
2862 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His compleynte, and for love his hoote fires,</B><BR>
2863 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He wolde make a fyr in which the office</B><BR>
2864 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Funeral he myghte al accomplice.</B><BR>
2865 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And leet comande anon to hakke and hewe</B><BR>
2866 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The okes olde, and leye hem on a rewe</B><BR>
2867 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In colpons wel arrayed for to brenne.</B><BR>
2868 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His officers with swifte feet they renne</B><BR>
2869 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And ryde anon at his comandement.</B><BR>
2870 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And after this, Theseus hath ysent</B><BR>
2871 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>After a beere, and it al overspradde</B><BR>
2872 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With clooth of gold, the richeste that he hadde.</B><BR>
2873 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And of the same suyte he cladde Arcite;</B><BR>
2874 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon his hondes hadde he gloves white,</B><BR>
2875 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Eek on his heed a coroune of laurer grene,</B><BR>
2876 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in his hond a swerd ful bright and kene.</B><BR>
2877 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He leyde hym, bare the visage, on the beere;</B><BR>
2878 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Therwith he weep that pitee was to heere.</B><BR>
2879 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And for the peple sholde seen hym alle,</B><BR>
2880 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan it was day, he broghte hym to the halle,</B><BR>
2881 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That roreth of the criyng and the soun.</B><BR>
2882 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Tho cam this woful Theban Palamoun,</B><BR>
2883 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With flotery berd and ruggy, asshy heeres,</B><BR>
2884 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In clothes blake, ydropped al with teeres;</B><BR>
2885 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And, passynge othere of wepynge, Emelye,</B><BR>
2886 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The rewefulleste of al the compaignye.</B><BR>
2887 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In as muche as the servyce sholde be</B><BR>
2888 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The moore noble and riche in his degree,</B><BR>
2889 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Duc Theseus leet forth thre steedes brynge,</B><BR>
2890 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That trapped were in steel al gliterynge,</B><BR>
2891 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And covered with the armes of daun Arcite.</B><BR>
2892 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon thise steedes, that weren grete and white,</B><BR>
2893 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther seten folk, of whiche oon baar his sheeld,</B><BR>
2894 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Another his spere up on his hondes heeld,</B><BR>
2895 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The thridde baar with hym his bowe Turkeys</B><BR>
2896 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>(Of brend gold was the caas and eek the harneys);</B><BR>
2897 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And riden forth a paas with sorweful cheere</B><BR>
2898 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Toward the grove, as ye shul after heere.</B><BR>
2899 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The nobleste of the Grekes that ther were</B><BR>
2900 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon hir shuldres caryeden the beere,</B><BR>
2901 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With slakke paas and eyen rede and wete,</B><BR>
2902 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thurghout the citee by the maister strete,</B><BR>
2903 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That sprad was al with blak, and wonder hye</B><BR>
2904 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Right of the same is the strete ywrye.</B><BR>
2905 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon the right hond wente olde Egeus,</B><BR>
2906 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And on that oother syde duc Theseus,</B><BR>
2907 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With vessels in hir hand of gold ful fyn,</B><BR>
2908 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al ful of hony, milk, and blood, and wyn;</B><BR>
2909 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Eek Palamon, with ful greet compaignye;</B><BR>
2910 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And after that cam woful Emelye,</B><BR>
2911 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With fyr in honde, as was that tyme the gyse,</B><BR>
2912 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To do the ritual of funeral service.</B><BR>
2913 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Heigh labour and ful greet apparaillynge</B><BR>
2914 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Was at the service and the fyr-makynge,</B><BR>
2915 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That with his grene top the hevene raughte;</B><BR>
2916 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And twenty fadme of brede the armes straughte --</B><BR>
2917 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This is to seyn, the bowes weren so brode.</B><BR>
2918 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of stree first ther was leyd ful many a lode.</B><BR>
2919 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But how the fyr was maked upon highte,</B><BR>
2920 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne eek the names that the trees highte,</B><BR>
2921 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As ook, firre, birch, aspe, alder, holm, popler,</B><BR>
2922 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wylugh, elm, plane, assh, box, chasteyn, lynde, laurer,</B><BR>
2923 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Mapul, thorn, bech, hasel, ew, whippeltree --</B><BR>
2924 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>How they weren feld shal nat be toold for me;</B><BR>
2925 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne hou the goddes ronnen up and doun,</B><BR>
2926 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Disherited of hire habitacioun,</B><BR>
2927 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In which they woneden in reste and pees,</B><BR>
2928 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Nymphes, fawnes and amadrides;</B><BR>
2929 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne hou the beestes and the briddes alle</B><BR>
2930 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Fledden for fere, whan the wode was falle;</B><BR>
2931 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne how the ground agast was of the light,</B><BR>
2932 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That was nat wont to seen the sonne bright;</B><BR>
2933 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne how the fyr was couched first with stree,</B><BR>
2934 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thanne with drye stikkes cloven a thre,</B><BR>
2935 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thanne with grene wode and spicerye,</B><BR>
2936 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thanne with clooth of gold and with perrye,</B><BR>
2937 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And gerlandes, hangynge with ful many a flour;</B><BR>
2938 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The mirre, th'encens, with al so greet odour;</B><BR>
2939 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne how Arcite lay among al this,</B><BR>
2940 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne what richesse aboute his body is;</B><BR>
2941 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne how that Emelye, as was the gyse,</B><BR>
2942 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Putte in the fyr of funeral servyse;</B><BR>
2943 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne how she swowned whan men made the fyr,</B><BR>
2944 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne what she spak, ne what was hir desir;</B><BR>
2945 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne what jeweles men in the fyre caste,</B><BR>
2946 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan that the fyr was greet and brente faste;</B><BR>
2947 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne how somme caste hir sheeld, and somme hir spere,</B><BR>
2948 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And of hire vestimentz, whiche that they were,</B><BR>
2949 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And coppes fulle of wyn, and milk, and blood,</B><BR>
2950 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Into the fyr, that brente as it were wood;</B><BR>
2951 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne how the Grekes, with an huge route,</B><BR>
2952 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thries riden al the fyr aboute</B><BR>
2953 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon the left hand, with a loud shoutynge,</B><BR>
2954 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thries with hir speres claterynge;</B><BR>
2955 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thries how the ladyes gonne crye;</B><BR>
2956 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And how that lad was homward Emelye;</B><BR>
2957 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne how Arcite is brent to asshen colde;</B><BR>
2958 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne how that lyche-wake was yholde</B><BR>
2959 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al thilke nyght; ne how the Grekes pleye</B><BR>
2960 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The wake-pleyes; ne kepe I nat to seye</B><BR>
2961 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Who wrastleth best naked with oille enoynt,</B><BR>
2962 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne who that baar hym best, in no disjoynt.</B><BR>
2963 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I wol nat tellen eek how that they goon</B><BR>
2964 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hoom til Atthenes, whan the pley is doon;</B><BR>
2965 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But shortly to the point thanne wol I wende</B><BR>
2966 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And maken of my longe tale an ende.</B><BR>
2967 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>By processe and by lengthe of certeyn yeres,</B><BR>
2968 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al stynted is the moornynge and the teres</B><BR>
2969 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of Grekes, by oon general assent.</B><BR>
2970 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne semed me ther was a parlement</B><BR>
2971 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>At Atthenes, upon certein pointz and caas;</B><BR>
2972 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Among the whiche pointz yspoken was,</B><BR>
2973 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To have with certein contrees alliaunce,</B><BR>
2974 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And have fully of Thebans obeisaunce.</B><BR>
2975 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For which this noble Theseus anon</B><BR>
2976 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Leet senden after gentil Palamon,</B><BR>
2977 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Unwist of hym what was the cause and why,</B><BR>
2978 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But in his blake clothes sorwefully</B><BR>
2979 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He cam at his comandement in hye.</B><BR>
2980 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Tho sente Theseus for Emelye.</B><BR>
2981 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan they were set, and hust was al the place,</B><BR>
2982 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Theseus abiden hadde a space</B><BR>
2983 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Er any word cam fram his wise brest,</B><BR>
2984 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His eyen sette he ther as was his lest.</B><BR>
2985 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with a sad visage he siked stille,</B><BR>
2986 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And after that right thus he seyde his wille:</B><BR>
2987 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"The Firste Moevere of the cause above,</B><BR>
2988 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan he first made the faire cheyne of love,</B><BR>
2989 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Greet was th'effect, and heigh was his entente.</B><BR>
2990 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wel wiste he why, and what thereof he mente,</B><BR>
2991 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For with that faire cheyne of love he bond</B><BR>
2992 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The fyr, the eyr, the water, and the lond</B><BR>
2993 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In certeyn boundes, that they may nat flee.</B><BR>
2994 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That same Prince and that Moevere," quod he,</B><BR>
2995 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Hath stablissed in this wrecched world adoun</B><BR>
2996 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Certeyne dayes and duracioun</B><BR>
2997 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To al that is engendred in this place,</B><BR>
2998 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Over the whiche day they may nat pace,</B><BR>
2999 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al mowe they yet tho dayes wel abregge.</B><BR>
3000 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther nedeth noght noon auctoritee t'allegge,</B><BR>
3001 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For it is preeved by experience,</B><BR>
3002 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But that me list declaren my sentence.</B><BR>
3003 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne may men by this ordre wel discerne</B><BR>
3004 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That thilke Moevere stable is and eterne.</B><BR>
3005 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wel may men knowe, but it be a fool,</B><BR>
3006 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That every part dirryveth from his hool,</B><BR>
3007 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For nature hath nat taken his bigynnyng</B><BR>
3008 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of no partie or cantel of a thyng,</B><BR>
3009 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But of a thyng that parfit is and stable,</B><BR>
3010 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Descendynge so til it be corrumpable.</B><BR>
3011 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And therfore, of his wise purveiaunce,</B><BR>
3012 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He hath so wel biset his ordinaunce</B><BR>
3013 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That speces of thynges and progressiouns</B><BR>
3014 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Shullen enduren by successiouns,</B><BR>
3015 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And nat eterne, withouten any lye.</B><BR>
3016 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This maystow understonde and seen at ye.</B><BR>
3017 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Loo the ook, that hath so long a norisshynge</B><BR>
3018 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>From tyme that it first bigynneth to sprynge,</B><BR>
3019 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And hath so long a lif, as we may see,</B><BR>
3020 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yet at the laste wasted is the tree.</B><BR>
3021 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Considereth eek how that the harde stoon</B><BR>
3022 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Under oure feet, on which we trede and goon,</B><BR>
3023 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yet wasteth it as it lyth by the weye.</B><BR>
3024 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The brode ryver somtyme wexeth dreye;</B><BR>
3025 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The grete tounes se we wane and wende.</B><BR>
3026 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne may ye se that al this thyng hath ende.</B><BR>
3027 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Of man and womman seen we wel also</B><BR>
3028 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That nedes, in oon of thise termes two --</B><BR>
3029 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This is to seyn, in youthe or elles age --</B><BR>
3030 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He moot be deed, the kyng as shal a page;</B><BR>
3031 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Som in his bed, som in the depe see,</B><BR>
3032 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Som in the large feeld, as men may see;</B><BR>
3033 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther helpeth noght; al goth that ilke weye.</B><BR>
3034 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne may I seyn that al this thyng moot deye.</B><BR>
3035 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"What maketh this but Juppiter, the kyng,</B><BR>
3036 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That is prince and cause of alle thyng,</B><BR>
3037 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Convertynge al unto his propre welle</B><BR>
3038 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>From which it is dirryved, sooth to telle?</B><BR>
3039 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And heer-agayns no creature on lyve,</B><BR>
3040 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of no degree, availleth for to stryve.</B><BR>
3041 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Thanne is it wysdom, as it thynketh me,</B><BR>
3042 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To maken vertu of necessitee,</B><BR>
3043 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And take it weel that we may nat eschue,</B><BR>
3044 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And namely that to us alle is due.</B><BR>
3045 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And whoso gruccheth ought, he dooth folye,</B><BR>
3046 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And rebel is to hym that al may gye.</B><BR>
3047 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And certeinly a man hath moost honour</B><BR>
3048 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To dyen in his excellence and flour,</B><BR>
3049 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan he is siker of his goode name;</B><BR>
3050 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne hath he doon his freend, ne hym, no shame.</B><BR>
3051 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And gladder oghte his freend been of his deeth,</B><BR>
3052 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan with honour up yolden is his breeth,</B><BR>
3053 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Than whan his name apalled is for age,</B><BR>
3054 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For al forgeten is his vassellage.</B><BR>
3055 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne is it best, as for a worthy fame,</B><BR>
3056 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To dyen whan that he is best of name.</B><BR>
3057 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"The contrarie of al this is wilfulnesse.</B><BR>
3058 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Why grucchen we, why have we hevynesse,</B><BR>
3059 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That goode Arcite, of chivalrie flour,</B><BR>
3060 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Departed is with duetee and honour</B><BR>
3061 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Out of this foule prisoun of this lyf?</B><BR>
3062 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Why grucchen heere his cosyn and his wyf</B><BR>
3063 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of his welfare, that loved hem so weel?</B><BR>
3064 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Kan he hem thank? Nay, God woot, never a deel,</B><BR>
3065 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That both his soule and eek hemself offende,</B><BR>
3066 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And yet they mowe hir lustes nat amende.</B><BR>
3067 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"What may I conclude of this longe serye,</B><BR>
3068 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But after wo I rede us to be merye</B><BR>
3069 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thanken Juppiter of al his grace?</B><BR>
3070 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And er that we departen from this place</B><BR>
3071 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I rede that we make of sorwes two</B><BR>
3072 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>O parfit joye, lastynge everemo.</B><BR>
3073 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And looketh now, wher moost sorwe is herinne,</B><BR>
3074 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther wol we first amenden and bigynne.</B><BR>
3075 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Suster," quod he, "this is my fulle assent,</B><BR>
3076 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With al th'avys heere of my parlement,</B><BR>
3077 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That gentil Palamon, youre owene knyght,</B><BR>
3078 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That serveth yow with wille, herte, and myght,</B><BR>
3079 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And ever hath doon syn ye first hym knewe,</B><BR>
3080 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That ye shul of youre grace upon hym rewe,</B><BR>
3081 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And taken hym for housbonde and for lord.</B><BR>
3082 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lene me youre hond, for this is oure accord.</B><BR>
3083 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lat se now of youre wommanly pitee.</B><BR>
3084 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He is a kynges brother sone, pardee;</B><BR>
3085 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And though he were a povre bacheler,</B><BR>
3086 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Syn he hath served yow so many a yeer,</B><BR>
3087 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And had for yow so greet adversitee,</B><BR>
3088 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>It moste been considered, leeveth me,</B><BR>
3089 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For gentil mercy oghte to passen right."</B><BR>
3090 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne seyde he thus to Palamon the knight:</B><BR>
3091 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"I trowe ther nedeth litel sermonyng</B><BR>
3092 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To make yow assente to this thyng.</B><BR>
3093 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Com neer, and taak youre lady by the hond."</B><BR>
3094 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bitwixen hem was maad anon the bond</B><BR>
3095 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That highte matrimoigne or mariage,</B><BR>
3096 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>By al the conseil and the baronage.</B><BR>
3097 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thus with alle blisse and melodye</B><BR>
3098 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hath Palamon ywedded Emelye.</B><BR>
3099 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And God, that al this wyde world hath wroght,</B><BR>
3100 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Sende hym his love that hath it deere aboght;</B><BR>
3101 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For now is Palamon in alle wele,</B><BR>
3102 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lyvynge in blisse, in richesse, and in heele,</B><BR>
3103 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Emelye hym loveth so tendrely,</B><BR>
3104 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And he hire serveth so gentilly,</B><BR>
3105 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That nevere was ther no word hem bitwene</B><BR>
3106 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of jalousie or any oother teene.</B><BR>
3107 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thus endeth Palamon and Emelye;</B><BR>
3108 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And God save al this faire compaignye! Amen.</B><BR>
1	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Whan that Aprill with his shoures soote</B><BR>
2	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The droghte of March hath perced to the roote,</B><BR>
3	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And bathed every veyne in swich licour</B><BR>
4	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of which vertu engendred is the flour;</B><BR>
5	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Whan Zephirus eek with his sweete breeth</B><BR>
6	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Inspired hath in every holt and heeth</B><BR>
7	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The tendre croppes, and the yonge sonne</B><BR>
8	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hath in the Ram his half cours yronne,</B><BR>
9	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And smale foweles maken melodye,</B><BR>
10	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That slepen al the nyght with open ye</B><BR>
11	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>(So priketh hem Nature in hir corages),</B><BR>
12	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Thanne longen folk to goon on pilgrimages,</B><BR>
13	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And palmeres for to seken straunge strondes,</B><BR>
14	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To ferne halwes, kowthe in sondry londes;</B><BR>
15	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And specially from every shires ende</B><BR>
16	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of Engelond to Caunterbury they wende,</B><BR>
17	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The hooly blisful martir for to seke,</B><BR>
18	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That hem hath holpen whan that they were seeke.</B><BR>
19	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Bifil that in that seson on a day,</B><BR>
20	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In Southwerk at the Tabard as I lay</B><BR>
21	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Redy to wenden on my pilgrymage</B><BR>
22	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To Caunterbury with ful devout corage,</B><BR>
23	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>At nyght was come into that hostelrye</B><BR>
24	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel nyne and twenty in a compaignye</B><BR>
25	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of sondry folk, by aventure yfalle</B><BR>
26	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In felaweshipe, and pilgrimes were they alle,</B><BR>
27	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That toward Caunterbury wolden ryde.</B><BR>
28	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The chambres and the stables weren wyde,</B><BR>
29	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And wel we weren esed atte beste.</B><BR>
30	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And shortly, whan the sonne was to reste,</B><BR>
31	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>So hadde I spoken with hem everichon</B><BR>
32	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That I was of hir felaweshipe anon,</B><BR>
33	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And made forward erly for to ryse,</B><BR>
34	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To take oure wey ther as I yow devyse.</B><BR>
35	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But nathelees, whil I have tyme and space,</B><BR>
36	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Er that I ferther in this tale pace,</B><BR>
37	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Me thynketh it acordaunt to resoun</B><BR>
38	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To telle yow al the condicioun</B><BR>
39	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of ech of hem, so as it semed me,</B><BR>
40	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And whiche they weren, and of what degree,</B><BR>
41	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And eek in what array that they were inne;</B><BR>
42	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And at a knyght than wol I first bigynne.</B><BR>
43	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A KNYGHT ther was, and that a worthy man,</B><BR>
44	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That fro the tyme that he first bigan</B><BR>
45	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To riden out, he loved chivalrie,</B><BR>
46	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Trouthe and honour, fredom and curteisie.</B><BR>
47	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful worthy was he in his lordes werre,</B><BR>
48	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And therto hadde he riden, no man ferre,</B><BR>
49	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>As wel in cristendom as in hethenesse,</B><BR>
50	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And evere honoured for his worthynesse;</B><BR>
51	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>At Alisaundre he was whan it was wonne.</B><BR>
52	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful ofte tyme he hadde the bord bigonne</B><BR>
53	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Aboven alle nacions in Pruce;</B><BR>
54	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In Lettow hadde he reysed and in Ruce,</B><BR>
55	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>No Cristen man so ofte of his degree.</B><BR>
56	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In Gernade at the seege eek hadde he be</B><BR>
57	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of Algezir, and riden in Belmarye.</B><BR>
58	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>At Lyeys was he and at Satalye,</B><BR>
59	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Whan they were wonne, and in the Grete See</B><BR>
60	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>At many a noble armee hadde he be.</B><BR>
61	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>At mortal batailles hadde he been fiftene,</B><BR>
62	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And foughten for oure feith at Tramyssene</B><BR>
63	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In lystes thries, and ay slayn his foo.</B><BR>
64	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>This ilke worthy knyght hadde been also</B><BR>
65	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Somtyme with the lord of Palatye</B><BR>
66	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Agayn another hethen in Turkye;</B><BR>
67	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And everemoore he hadde a sovereyn prys.</B><BR>
68	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And though that he were worthy, he was wys,</B><BR>
69	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And of his port as meeke as is a mayde.</B><BR>
70	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He nevere yet no vileynye ne sayde</B><BR>
71	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In al his lyf unto no maner wight.</B><BR>
72	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was a verray, parfit gentil knyght.</B><BR>
73	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But for to tellen yow of his array,</B><BR>
74	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His hors were goode, but he was nat gay.</B><BR>
75	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of fustian he wered a gypon</B><BR>
76	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Al bismotered with his habergeon,</B><BR>
77	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For he was late ycome from his viage,</B><BR>
78	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And wente for to doon his pilgrymage.</B><BR>
79	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With hym ther was his sone, a yong SQUIER,</B><BR>
80	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A lovyere and a lusty bacheler,</B><BR>
81	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With lokkes crulle as they were leyd in presse.</B><BR>
82	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of twenty yeer of age he was, I gesse.</B><BR>
83	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of his stature he was of evene lengthe,</B><BR>
84	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And wonderly delyvere, and of greet strengthe.</B><BR>
85	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And he hadde been somtyme in chyvachie</B><BR>
86	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In Flaundres, in Artoys, and Pycardie,</B><BR>
87	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And born hym weel, as of so litel space,</B><BR>
88	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In hope to stonden in his lady grace.</B><BR>
89	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Embrouded was he, as it were a meede</B><BR>
90	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Al ful of fresshe floures, whyte and reede.</B><BR>
91	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Syngynge he was, or floytynge, al the day;</B><BR>
92	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was as fressh as is the month of May.</B><BR>
93	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Short was his gowne, with sleves longe and wyde.</B><BR>
94	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel koude he sitte on hors and faire ryde.</B><BR>
95	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He koude songes make and wel endite,</B><BR>
96	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Juste and eek daunce, and weel purtreye and write.</B><BR>
97	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>So hoote he lovede that by nyghtertale</B><BR>
98	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He sleep namoore than dooth a nyghtyngale.</B><BR>
99	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Curteis he was, lowely, and servysable,</B><BR>
100	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And carf biforn his fader at the table.</B><BR>
101	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A YEMAN hadde he and servantz namo</B><BR>
102	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>At that tyme, for hym liste ride so,</B><BR>
103	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And he was clad in cote and hood of grene.</B><BR>
104	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A sheef of pecok arwes, bright and kene,</B><BR>
105	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Under his belt he bar ful thriftily</B><BR>
106	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>(Wel koude he dresse his takel yemanly;</B><BR>
107	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His arwes drouped noght with fetheres lowe),</B><BR>
108	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And in his hand he baar a myghty bowe.</B><BR>
109	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A not heed hadde he, with a broun visage.</B><BR>
110	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of wodecraft wel koude he al the usage.</B><BR>
111	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Upon his arm he baar a gay bracer,</B><BR>
112	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And by his syde a swerd and a bokeler,</B><BR>
113	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And on that oother syde a gay daggere</B><BR>
114	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Harneised wel and sharp as point of spere;</B><BR>
115	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A Cristopher on his brest of silver sheene.</B><BR>
116	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>An horn he bar, the bawdryk was of grene;</B><BR>
117	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A forster was he, soothly, as I gesse.</B><BR>
118	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther was also a Nonne, a PRIORESSE,</B><BR>
119	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That of hir smylyng was ful symple and coy;</B><BR>
120	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hire gretteste ooth was but by Seinte Loy;</B><BR>
121	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And she was cleped madame Eglentyne.</B><BR>
122	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful weel she soong the service dyvyne,</B><BR>
123	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Entuned in hir nose ful semely;</B><BR>
124	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And Frenssh she spak ful faire and fetisly,</B><BR>
125	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>After the scole of Stratford atte Bowe,</B><BR>
126	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For Frenssh of Parys was to hire unknowe.</B><BR>
127	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>At mete wel ytaught was she with alle;</B><BR>
128	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>She leet no morsel from hir lippes falle,</B><BR>
129	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ne wette hir fyngres in hir sauce depe;</B><BR>
130	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel koude she carie a morsel and wel kepe</B><BR>
131	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That no drope ne fille upon hire brest.</B><BR>
132	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In curteisie was set ful muchel hir lest.</B><BR>
133	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hir over-lippe wyped she so clene</B><BR>
134	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That in hir coppe ther was no ferthyng sene</B><BR>
135	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of grece, whan she dronken hadde hir draughte.</B><BR>
136	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful semely after hir mete she raughte.</B><BR>
137	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And sikerly she was of greet desport,</B><BR>
138	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And ful plesaunt, and amyable of port,</B><BR>
139	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And peyned hire to countrefete cheere</B><BR>
140	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of court, and to been estatlich of manere,</B><BR>
141	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And to ben holden digne of reverence.</B><BR>
142	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But for to speken of hire conscience,</B><BR>
143	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>She was so charitable and so pitous</B><BR>
144	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>She wolde wepe, if that she saugh a mous</B><BR>
145	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Kaught in a trappe, if it were deed or bledde.</B><BR>
146	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of smale houndes hadde she that she fedde</B><BR>
147	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With rosted flessh, or milk and wastel-breed.</B><BR>
148	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But soore wepte she if oon of hem were deed,</B><BR>
149	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Or if men smoot it with a yerde smerte;</B><BR>
150	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And al was conscience and tendre herte.</B><BR>
151	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful semyly hir wympul pynched was,</B><BR>
152	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hir nose tretys, hir eyen greye as glas,</B><BR>
153	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hir mouth ful smal, and therto softe and reed.</B><BR>
154	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But sikerly she hadde a fair forheed;</B><BR>
155	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>It was almoost a spanne brood, I trowe;</B><BR>
156	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For, hardily, she was nat undergrowe.</B><BR>
157	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful fetys was hir cloke, as I was war.</B><BR>
158	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of smal coral aboute hire arm she bar</B><BR>
159	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A peire of bedes, gauded al with grene,</B><BR>
160	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And theron heng a brooch of gold ful sheene,</B><BR>
161	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>On which ther was first write a crowned A,</B><BR>
162	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And after Amor vincit omnia.</B><BR>
163	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Another NONNE with hire hadde she,</B><BR>
164	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That was hir chapeleyne, and preestes thre.</B><BR>
165	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A MONK ther was, a fair for the maistrie,</B><BR>
166	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>An outridere, that lovede venerie,</B><BR>
167	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A manly man, to been an abbot able.</B><BR>
168	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful many a deyntee hors hadde he in stable,</B><BR>
169	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And whan he rood, men myghte his brydel heere</B><BR>
170	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Gynglen in a whistlynge wynd als cleere</B><BR>
171	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And eek as loude as dooth the chapel belle</B><BR>
172	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther as this lord was kepere of the celle.</B><BR>
173	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The reule of Seint Maure or of Seint Beneit --</B><BR>
174	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>By cause that it was old and somdel streit</B><BR>
175	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>This ilke Monk leet olde thynges pace,</B><BR>
176	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And heeld after the newe world the space.</B><BR>
177	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He yaf nat of that text a pulled hen,</B><BR>
178	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That seith that hunters ben nat hooly men,</B><BR>
179	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ne that a monk, whan he is recchelees,</B><BR>
180	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Is likned til a fissh that is waterlees --</B><BR>
181	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>This is to seyn, a monk out of his cloystre.</B><BR>
182	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But thilke text heeld he nat worth an oystre;</B><BR>
183	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And I seyde his opinion was good.</B><BR>
184	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>What sholde he studie and make hymselven wood,</B><BR>
185	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Upon a book in cloystre alwey to poure,</B><BR>
186	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Or swynken with his handes, and laboure,</B><BR>
187	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>As Austyn bit? How shal the world be served?</B><BR>
188	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Lat Austyn have his swynk to hym reserved!</B><BR>
189	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Therfore he was a prikasour aright:</B><BR>
190	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Grehoundes he hadde as swift as fowel in flight;</B><BR>
191	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of prikyng and of huntyng for the hare</B><BR>
192	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Was al his lust, for no cost wolde he spare.</B><BR>
193	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>I seigh his sleves purfiled at the hond</B><BR>
194	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With grys, and that the fyneste of a lond;</B><BR>
195	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And for to festne his hood under his chyn,</B><BR>
196	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He hadde of gold ywroght a ful curious pyn;</B><BR>
197	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A love-knotte in the gretter ende ther was.</B><BR>
198	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His heed was balled, that shoon as any glas,</B><BR>
199	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And eek his face, as he hadde been enoynt.</B><BR>
200	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was a lord ful fat and in good poynt;</B><BR>
201	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His eyen stepe, and rollynge in his heed,</B><BR>
202	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That stemed as a forneys of a leed;</B><BR>
203	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His bootes souple, his hors in greet estaat.</B><BR>
204	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Now certeinly he was a fair prelaat;</B><BR>
205	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was nat pale as a forpyned goost.</B><BR>
206	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A fat swan loved he best of any roost.</B><BR>
207	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His palfrey was as broun as is a berye.</B><BR>
208	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A FRERE ther was, a wantowne and a merye,</B><BR>
209	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A lymytour, a ful solempne man.</B><BR>
210	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In alle the ordres foure is noon that kan</B><BR>
211	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>So muchel of daliaunce and fair langage.</B><BR>
212	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He hadde maad ful many a mariage</B><BR>
213	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of yonge wommen at his owene cost.</B><BR>
214	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Unto his ordre he was a noble post.</B><BR>
215	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful wel biloved and famulier was he</B><BR>
216	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With frankeleyns over al in his contree,</B><BR>
217	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And eek with worthy wommen of the toun;</B><BR>
218	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For he hadde power of confessioun,</B><BR>
219	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>As seyde hymself, moore than a curat,</B><BR>
220	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For of his ordre he was licenciat.</B><BR>
221	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful swetely herde he confessioun,</B><BR>
222	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And plesaunt was his absolucioun:</B><BR>
223	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was an esy man to yeve penaunce,</B><BR>
224	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther as he wiste to have a good pitaunce.</B><BR>
225	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For unto a povre ordre for to yive</B><BR>
226	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Is signe that a man is wel yshryve;</B><BR>
227	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For if he yaf, he dorste make avaunt,</B><BR>
228	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He wiste that a man was repentaunt;</B><BR>
229	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For many a man so hard is of his herte,</B><BR>
230	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He may nat wepe, althogh hym soore smerte.</B><BR>
231	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Therfore in stede of wepynge and preyeres</B><BR>
232	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Men moote yeve silver to the povre freres.</B><BR>
233	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His typet was ay farsed ful of knyves</B><BR>
234	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And pynnes, for to yeven faire wyves.</B><BR>
235	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And certeinly he hadde a murye note:</B><BR>
236	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel koude he synge and pleyen on a rote;</B><BR>
237	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of yeddynges he baar outrely the pris.</B><BR>
238	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His nekke whit was as the flour-de-lys;</B><BR>
239	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Therto he strong was as a champioun.</B><BR>
240	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He knew the tavernes wel in every toun</B><BR>
241	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And everich hostiler and tappestere</B><BR>
242	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Bet than a lazar or a beggestere,</B><BR>
243	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For unto swich a worthy man as he</B><BR>
244	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Acorded nat, as by his facultee,</B><BR>
245	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To have with sike lazars aqueyntaunce.</B><BR>
246	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>It is nat honest; it may nat avaunce,</B><BR>
247	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For to deelen with no swich poraille,</B><BR>
248	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But al with riche and selleres of vitaille.</B><BR>
249	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And over al, ther as profit sholde arise,</B><BR>
250	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Curteis he was and lowely of servyse;</B><BR>
251	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther nas no man nowher so vertuous.</B><BR>
252	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was the beste beggere in his hous;</B><BR>
252a	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>[And yaf a certeyn ferme for the graunt; </B><BR>
252a	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Noon of his bretheren cam ther in his haunt;] </B><BR>
253	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For thogh a wydwe hadde noght a sho,</B><BR>
254	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>So plesaunt was his "In principio,"</B><BR>
255	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Yet wolde he have a ferthyng, er he wente.</B><BR>
256	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His purchas was wel bettre than his rente.</B><BR>
257	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And rage he koude, as it were right a whelp.</B><BR>
258	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In love-dayes ther koude he muchel help,</B><BR>
259	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For ther he was nat lyk a cloysterer</B><BR>
260	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With a thredbare cope, as is a povre scoler,</B><BR>
261	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But he was lyk a maister or a pope.</B><BR>
262	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of double worstede was his semycope,</B><BR>
263	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That rounded as a belle out of the presse.</B><BR>
264	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Somwhat he lipsed, for his wantownesse,</B><BR>
265	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To make his Englissh sweete upon his tonge;</B><BR>
266	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And in his harpyng, whan that he hadde songe,</B><BR>
267	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His eyen twynkled in his heed aryght</B><BR>
268	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>As doon the sterres in the frosty nyght.</B><BR>
269	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>This worthy lymytour was cleped Huberd.</B><BR>
270	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A MARCHANT was ther with a forked berd,</B><BR>
271	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In mottelee, and hye on horse he sat;</B><BR>
272	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Upon his heed a Flaundryssh bever hat,</B><BR>
273	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His bootes clasped faire and fetisly.</B><BR>
274	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His resons he spak ful solempnely,</B><BR>
275	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Sownynge alwey th' encrees of his wynnyng.</B><BR>
276	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He wolde the see were kept for any thyng</B><BR>
277	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Bitwixe Middelburgh and Orewelle.</B><BR>
278	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel koude he in eschaunge sheeldes selle.</B><BR>
279	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>This worthy man ful wel his wit bisette:</B><BR>
280	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther wiste no wight that he was in dette,</B><BR>
281	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>So estatly was he of his governaunce</B><BR>
282	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With his bargaynes and with his chevyssaunce.</B><BR>
283	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For sothe he was a worthy man with alle,</B><BR>
284	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But, sooth to seyn, I noot how men hym calle.</B><BR>
285	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A CLERK ther was of Oxenford also,</B><BR>
286	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That unto logyk hadde longe ygo.</B><BR>
287	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>As leene was his hors as is a rake,</B><BR>
288	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And he nas nat right fat, I undertake,</B><BR>
289	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But looked holwe, and therto sobrely.</B><BR>
290	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful thredbare was his overeste courtepy,</B><BR>
291	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For he hadde geten hym yet no benefice,</B><BR>
292	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ne was so worldly for to have office.</B><BR>
293	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For hym was levere have at his beddes heed</B><BR>
294	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Twenty bookes, clad in blak or reed,</B><BR>
295	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of Aristotle and his philosophie</B><BR>
296	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Than robes riche, or fithele, or gay sautrie.</B><BR>
297	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But al be that he was a philosophre,</B><BR>
298	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Yet hadde he but litel gold in cofre;</B><BR>
299	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But al that he myghte of his freendes hente,</B><BR>
300	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>On bookes and on lernynge he it spente,</B><BR>
301	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And bisily gan for the soules preye</B><BR>
302	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of hem that yaf hym wherwith to scoleye.</B><BR>
303	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of studie took he moost cure and moost heede.</B><BR>
304	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Noght o word spak he moore than was neede,</B><BR>
305	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And that was seyd in forme and reverence,</B><BR>
306	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And short and quyk and ful of hy sentence;</B><BR>
307	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Sownynge in moral vertu was his speche,</B><BR>
308	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And gladly wolde he lerne and gladly teche.</B><BR>
309	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A SERGEANT OF THE LAWE, war and wys,</B><BR>
310	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That often hadde been at the Parvys,</B><BR>
311	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther was also, ful riche of excellence.</B><BR>
312	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Discreet he was and of greet reverence --</B><BR>
313	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He semed swich, his wordes weren so wise.</B><BR>
314	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Justice he was ful often in assise,</B><BR>
315	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>By patente and by pleyn commissioun.</B><BR>
316	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For his science and for his heigh renoun,</B><BR>
317	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of fees and robes hadde he many oon.</B><BR>
318	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>So greet a purchasour was nowher noon:</B><BR>
319	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Al was fee symple to hym in effect;</B><BR>
320	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His purchasyng myghte nat been infect.</B><BR>
321	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Nowher so bisy a man as he ther nas,</B><BR>
322	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And yet he semed bisier than he was.</B><BR>
323	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In termes hadde he caas and doomes alle</B><BR>
324	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That from the tyme of kyng William were falle.</B><BR>
325	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Therto he koude endite and make a thyng,</B><BR>
326	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther koude no wight pynche at his writyng;</B><BR>
327	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And every statut koude he pleyn by rote.</B><BR>
328	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He rood but hoomly in a medlee cote,</B><BR>
329	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Girt with a ceint of silk, with barres smale;</B><BR>
330	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of his array telle I no lenger tale.</B><BR>
331	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A FRANKELEYN was in his compaignye.</B><BR>
332	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Whit was his berd as is the dayesye;</B><BR>
333	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of his complexioun he was sangwyn.</B><BR>
334	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel loved he by the morwe a sop in wyn;</B><BR>
335	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To lyven in delit was evere his wone,</B><BR>
336	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For he was Epicurus owene sone,</B><BR>
