337	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That heeld opinioun that pleyn delit</B><BR>
338	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Was verray felicitee parfit.</B><BR>
339	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>An housholdere, and that a greet, was he;</B><BR>
340	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Seint Julian he was in his contree.</B><BR>
341	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His breed, his ale, was alweys after oon;</B><BR>
342	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A bettre envyned man was nowher noon.</B><BR>
343	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Withoute bake mete was nevere his hous,</B><BR>
344	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of fissh and flessh, and that so plentevous</B><BR>
345	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>It snewed in his hous of mete and drynke;</B><BR>
346	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of alle deyntees that men koude thynke,</B><BR>
347	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>After the sondry sesons of the yeer,</B><BR>
348	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>So chaunged he his mete and his soper.</B><BR>
349	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful many a fat partrich hadde he in muwe,</B><BR>
350	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And many a breem and many a luce in stuwe.</B><BR>
351	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wo was his cook but if his sauce were</B><BR>
352	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Poynaunt and sharp, and redy al his geere.</B><BR>
353	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His table dormant in his halle alway</B><BR>
354	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Stood redy covered al the longe day.</B><BR>
355	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>At sessiouns ther was he lord and sire;</B><BR>
356	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful ofte tyme he was knyght of the shire.</B><BR>
357	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>An anlaas and a gipser al of silk</B><BR>
358	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Heeng at his girdel, whit as morne milk.</B><BR>
359	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A shirreve hadde he been, and a contour.</B><BR>
360	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Was nowher swich a worthy vavasour.</B><BR>
361	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>AN HABERDASSHERE and a CARPENTER,</B><BR>
362	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A WEBBE, a DYERE, and a TAPYCER --</B><BR>
363	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And they were clothed alle in o lyveree</B><BR>
364	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of a solempne and a greet fraternitee.</B><BR>
365	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful fressh and newe hir geere apiked was;</B><BR>
366	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hir knyves were chaped noght with bras</B><BR>
367	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But al with silver, wroght ful clene and weel,</B><BR>
368	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hire girdles and hir pouches everydeel.</B><BR>
369	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel semed ech of hem a fair burgeys</B><BR>
370	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To sitten in a yeldehalle on a deys.</B><BR>
371	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Everich, for the wisdom that he kan,</B><BR>
372	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Was shaply for to been an alderman.</B><BR>
373	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For catel hadde they ynogh and rente,</B><BR>
374	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And eek hir wyves wolde it wel assente;</B><BR>
375	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And elles certeyn were they to blame.</B><BR>
376	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>It is ful fair to been ycleped "madame,"</B><BR>
377	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And goon to vigilies al bifore,</B><BR>
378	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And have a mantel roialliche ybore.</B><BR>
379	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A COOK they hadde with hem for the nones</B><BR>
380	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To boille the chiknes with the marybones,</B><BR>
381	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And poudre-marchant tart and galyngale.</B><BR>
382	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel koude he knowe a draughte of Londoun ale.</B><BR>
383	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He koude rooste, and sethe, and broille, and frye,</B><BR>
384	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Maken mortreux, and wel bake a pye.</B><BR>
385	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But greet harm was it, as it thoughte me,</B><BR>
386	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That on his shyne a mormal hadde he.</B><BR>
387	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For blankmanger, that made he with the beste.</B><BR>
388	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A SHIPMAN was ther, wonynge fer by weste;</B><BR>
389	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For aught I woot, he was of Dertemouthe.</B><BR>
390	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He rood upon a rouncy, as he kouthe,</B><BR>
391	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In a gowne of faldyng to the knee.</B><BR>
392	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A daggere hangynge on a laas hadde he</B><BR>
393	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Aboute his nekke, under his arm adoun.</B><BR>
394	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The hoote somer hadde maad his hewe al broun;</B><BR>
395	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And certeinly he was a good felawe.</B><BR>
396	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful many a draughte of wyn had he ydrawe</B><BR>
397	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Fro Burdeux-ward, whil that the chapman sleep.</B><BR>
398	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of nyce conscience took he no keep.</B><BR>
399	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>If that he faught and hadde the hyer hond,</B><BR>
400	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>By water he sente hem hoom to every lond.</B><BR>
401	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But of his craft to rekene wel his tydes,</B><BR>
402	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His stremes, and his daungers hym bisides,</B><BR>
403	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His herberwe, and his moone, his lodemenage,</B><BR>
404	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther nas noon swich from Hulle to Cartage.</B><BR>
405	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hardy he was and wys to undertake;</B><BR>
406	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With many a tempest hadde his berd been shake.</B><BR>
407	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He knew alle the havenes, as they were,</B><BR>
408	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Fro Gootlond to the cape of Fynystere,</B><BR>
409	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And every cryke in Britaigne and in Spayne.</B><BR>
410	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His barge ycleped was the Maudelayne.</B><BR>
411	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With us ther was a DOCTOUR OF PHISIK;</B><BR>
412	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In al this world ne was ther noon hym lik,</B><BR>
413	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To speke of phisik and of surgerye,</B><BR>
414	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For he was grounded in astronomye.</B><BR>
415	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He kepte his pacient a ful greet deel</B><BR>
416	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In houres by his magyk natureel.</B><BR>
417	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel koude he fortunen the ascendent</B><BR>
418	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of his ymages for his pacient.</B><BR>
419	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He knew the cause of everich maladye,</B><BR>
420	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Were it of hoot, or coold, or moyste, or drye,</B><BR>
421	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And where they engendred, and of what humour.</B><BR>
422	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was a verray, parfit praktisour:</B><BR>
423	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The cause yknowe, and of his harm the roote,</B><BR>
424	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Anon he yaf the sike man his boote.</B><BR>
425	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful redy hadde he his apothecaries</B><BR>
426	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To sende hym drogges and his letuaries,</B><BR>
427	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For ech of hem made oother for to wynne --</B><BR>
428	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hir frendshipe nas nat newe to bigynne.</B><BR>
429	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel knew he the olde Esculapius,</B><BR>
430	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And Deyscorides, and eek Rufus,</B><BR>
431	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Olde Ypocras, Haly, and Galyen,</B><BR>
432	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Serapion, Razis, and Avycen,</B><BR>
433	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Averrois, Damascien, and Constantyn,</B><BR>
434	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Bernard, and Gatesden, and Gilbertyn.</B><BR>
435	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of his diete mesurable was he,</B><BR>
436	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For it was of no superfluitee,</B><BR>
437	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But of greet norissyng and digestible.</B><BR>
438	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His studie was but litel on the Bible.</B><BR>
439	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In sangwyn and in pers he clad was al,</B><BR>
440	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Lyned with taffata and with sendal.</B><BR>
441	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And yet he was but esy of dispence;</B><BR>
442	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He kepte that he wan in pestilence.</B><BR>
443	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For gold in phisik is a cordial,</B><BR>
444	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Therefore he lovede gold in special.</B><BR>
445	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A good WIF was ther OF biside BATHE,</B><BR>
446	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But she was somdel deef, and that was scathe.</B><BR>
447	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of clooth-makyng she hadde swich an haunt</B><BR>
448	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>She passed hem of Ypres and of Gaunt.</B><BR>
449	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In al the parisshe wif ne was ther noon</B><BR>
450	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That to the offrynge bifore hire sholde goon;</B><BR>
451	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And if ther dide, certeyn so wrooth was she</B><BR>
452	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That she was out of alle charitee.</B><BR>
453	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hir coverchiefs ful fyne weren of ground;</B><BR>
454	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>I dorste swere they weyeden ten pound</B><BR>
455	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That on a Sonday weren upon hir heed.</B><BR>
456	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hir hosen weren of fyn scarlet reed,</B><BR>
457	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful streite yteyd, and shoes ful moyste and newe.</B><BR>
458	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Boold was hir face, and fair, and reed of hewe.</B><BR>
459	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>She was a worthy womman al hir lyve:</B><BR>
460	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Housbondes at chirche dore she hadde fyve,</B><BR>
461	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Withouten oother compaignye in youthe --</B><BR>
462	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But thereof nedeth nat to speke as nowthe.</B><BR>
463	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And thries hadde she been at Jerusalem;</B><BR>
464	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>She hadde passed many a straunge strem;</B><BR>
465	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>At Rome she hadde been, and at Boloigne,</B><BR>
466	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In Galice at Seint-Jame, and at Coloigne.</B><BR>
467	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>She koude muchel of wandrynge by the weye.</B><BR>
468	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Gat-tothed was she, soothly for to seye.</B><BR>
469	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Upon an amblere esily she sat,</B><BR>
470	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ywympled wel, and on hir heed an hat</B><BR>
471	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>As brood as is a bokeler or a targe;</B><BR>
472	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A foot-mantel aboute hir hipes large,</B><BR>
473	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And on hir feet a paire of spores sharpe.</B><BR>
474	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In felaweshipe wel koude she laughe and carpe.</B><BR>
475	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of remedies of love she knew per chaunce,</B><BR>
476	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For she koude of that art the olde daunce.</B><BR>
477	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A good man was ther of religioun,</B><BR>
478	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And was a povre PERSOUN OF A TOUN,</B><BR>
479	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But riche he was of hooly thoght and werk.</B><BR>
480	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was also a lerned man, a clerk,</B><BR>
481	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That Cristes gospel trewely wolde preche;</B><BR>
482	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His parisshens devoutly wolde he teche.</B><BR>
483	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Benygne he was, and wonder diligent,</B><BR>
484	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And in adversitee ful pacient,</B><BR>
485	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And swich he was ypreved ofte sithes.</B><BR>
486	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful looth were hym to cursen for his tithes,</B><BR>
487	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But rather wolde he yeven, out of doute,</B><BR>
488	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Unto his povre parisshens aboute</B><BR>
489	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of his offryng and eek of his substaunce.</B><BR>
490	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He koude in litel thyng have suffisaunce.</B><BR>
491	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wyd was his parisshe, and houses fer asonder,</B><BR>
492	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But he ne lefte nat, for reyn ne thonder,</B><BR>
493	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In siknesse nor in meschief to visite</B><BR>
494	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The ferreste in his parisshe, muche and lite,</B><BR>
495	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Upon his feet, and in his hand a staf.</B><BR>
496	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>This noble ensample to his sheep he yaf,</B><BR>
497	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That first he wroghte, and afterward he taughte.</B><BR>
498	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Out of the gospel he tho wordes caughte,</B><BR>
499	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And this figure he added eek therto,</B><BR>
500	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That if gold ruste, what shal iren do?</B><BR>
501	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For if a preest be foul, on whom we truste,</B><BR>
502	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>No wonder is a lewed man to ruste;</B><BR>
503	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And shame it is, if a prest take keep,</B><BR>
504	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A shiten shepherde and a clene sheep.</B><BR>
505	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel oghte a preest ensample for to yive,</B><BR>
506	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>By his clennesse, how that his sheep sholde lyve.</B><BR>
507	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He sette nat his benefice to hyre</B><BR>
508	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And leet his sheep encombred in the myre</B><BR>
509	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And ran to Londoun unto Seinte Poules</B><BR>
510	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To seken hym a chaunterie for soules,</B><BR>
511	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Or with a bretherhed to been withholde;</B><BR>
512	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But dwelte at hoom, and kepte wel his folde,</B><BR>
513	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>So that the wolf ne made it nat myscarie;</B><BR>
514	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was a shepherde and noght a mercenarie.</B><BR>
515	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And though he hooly were and vertuous,</B><BR>
516	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was to synful men nat despitous,</B><BR>
517	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ne of his speche daungerous ne digne,</B><BR>
518	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But in his techyng discreet and benygne.</B><BR>
519	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To drawen folk to hevene by fairnesse,</B><BR>
520	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>By good ensample, this was his bisynesse.</B><BR>
521	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But it were any persone obstinat,</B><BR>
522	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>What so he were, of heigh or lough estat,</B><BR>
523	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hym wolde he snybben sharply for the nonys.</B><BR>
524	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A bettre preest I trowe that nowher noon ys.</B><BR>
525	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He waited after no pompe and reverence,</B><BR>
526	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ne maked him a spiced conscience,</B><BR>
527	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But Cristes loore and his apostles twelve</B><BR>
528	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He taughte; but first he folwed it hymselve.</B><BR>
529	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With hym ther was a PLOWMAN, was his brother,</B><BR>
530	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That hadde ylad of dong ful many a fother;</B><BR>
531	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A trewe swynkere and a good was he,</B><BR>
532	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Lyvynge in pees and parfit charitee.</B><BR>
533	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>God loved he best with al his hoole herte</B><BR>
534	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>At alle tymes, thogh him gamed or smerte,</B><BR>
535	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And thanne his neighebor right as hymselve.</B><BR>
536	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He wolde thresshe, and therto dyke and delve,</B><BR>
537	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For Cristes sake, for every povre wight,</B><BR>
538	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Withouten hire, if it lay in his myght.</B><BR>
539	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His tithes payde he ful faire and wel,</B><BR>
540	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Bothe of his propre swynk and his catel.</B><BR>
541	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In a tabard he rood upon a mere.</B><BR>
542	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther was also a REVE, and a MILLERE,</B><BR>
543	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A SOMNOUR, and a PARDONER also,</B><BR>
544	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A MAUNCIPLE, and myself -- ther were namo.</B><BR>
545	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The MILLERE was a stout carl for the nones;</B><BR>
546	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful byg he was of brawn, and eek of bones.</B><BR>
547	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That proved wel, for over al ther he cam,</B><BR>
548	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>At wrastlynge he wolde have alwey the ram.</B><BR>
549	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was short-sholdred, brood, a thikke knarre;</B><BR>
550	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther was no dore that he nolde heve of harre,</B><BR>
551	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Or breke it at a rennyng with his heed.</B><BR>
552	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His berd as any sowe or fox was reed,</B><BR>
553	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And therto brood, as though it were a spade.</B><BR>
554	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Upon the cop right of his nose he hade</B><BR>
555	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A werte, and theron stood a toft of herys,</B><BR>
556	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Reed as the brustles of a sowes erys;</B><BR>
557	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His nosethirles blake were and wyde.</B><BR>
558	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A swerd and a bokeler bar he by his syde.</B><BR>
559	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His mouth as greet was as a greet forneys.</B><BR>
560	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was a janglere and a goliardeys,</B><BR>
561	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And that was moost of synne and harlotries.</B><BR>
562	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel koude he stelen corn and tollen thries;</B><BR>
563	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And yet he hadde a thombe of gold, pardee.</B><BR>
564	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A whit cote and a blew hood wered he.</B><BR>
565	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A baggepipe wel koude he blowe and sowne,</B><BR>
566	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And therwithal he broghte us out of towne.</B><BR>
567	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A gentil MAUNCIPLE was ther of a temple,</B><BR>
568	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of which achatours myghte take exemple</B><BR>
569	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For to be wise in byynge of vitaille;</B><BR>
570	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For wheither that he payde or took by taille,</B><BR>
571	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Algate he wayted so in his achaat</B><BR>
572	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That he was ay biforn and in good staat.</B><BR>
573	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Now is nat that of God a ful fair grace</B><BR>
574	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That swich a lewed mannes wit shal pace</B><BR>
575	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The wisdom of an heep of lerned men?</B><BR>
576	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of maistres hadde he mo than thries ten,</B><BR>
577	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That weren of lawe expert and curious,</B><BR>
578	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of which ther were a duszeyne in that hous</B><BR>
579	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Worthy to been stywardes of rente and lond</B><BR>
580	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of any lord that is in Engelond,</B><BR>
581	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To make hym lyve by his propre good</B><BR>
582	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In honour dettelees (but if he were wood),</B><BR>
583	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Or lyve as scarsly as hym list desire;</B><BR>
584	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And able for to helpen al a shire</B><BR>
585	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In any caas that myghte falle or happe.</B><BR>
586	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And yet this Manciple sette hir aller cappe.</B><BR>
587	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The REVE was a sclendre colerik man.</B><BR>
588	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His berd was shave as ny as ever he kan;</B><BR>
589	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His heer was by his erys ful round yshorn;</B><BR>
590	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His top was dokked lyk a preest biforn.</B><BR>
591	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful longe were his legges and ful lene,</B><BR>
592	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ylyk a staf; ther was no calf ysene.</B><BR>
593	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel koude he kepe a gerner and a bynne;</B><BR>
594	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther was noon auditour koude on him wynne.</B><BR>
595	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel wiste he by the droghte and by the reyn</B><BR>
596	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The yeldynge of his seed and of his greyn.</B><BR>
597	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His lordes sheep, his neet, his dayerye,</B><BR>
598	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His swyn, his hors, his stoor, and his pultrye</B><BR>
599	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Was hoolly in this Reves governynge,</B><BR>
600	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And by his covenant yaf the rekenynge,</B><BR>
601	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Syn that his lord was twenty yeer of age.</B><BR>
602	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther koude no man brynge hym in arrerage.</B><BR>
603	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther nas baillif, ne hierde, nor oother hyne,</B><BR>
604	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That he ne knew his sleighte and his covyne;</B><BR>
605	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>They were adrad of hym as of the deeth.</B><BR>
606	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His wonyng was ful faire upon an heeth;</B><BR>
607	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With grene trees yshadwed was his place.</B><BR>
608	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He koude bettre than his lord purchace.</B><BR>
609	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful riche he was astored pryvely.</B><BR>
610	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His lord wel koude he plesen subtilly,</B><BR>
611	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To yeve and lene hym of his owene good,</B><BR>
612	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And have a thank, and yet a cote and hood.</B><BR>
613	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In youthe he hadde lerned a good myster:</B><BR>
614	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was a wel good wrighte, a carpenter.</B><BR>
615	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>This Reve sat upon a ful good stot</B><BR>
616	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That was al pomely grey and highte Scot.</B><BR>
617	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A long surcote of pers upon he hade,</B><BR>
618	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And by his syde he baar a rusty blade.</B><BR>
619	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of Northfolk was this Reve of which I telle,</B><BR>
620	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Biside a toun men clepen Baldeswelle.</B><BR>
621	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Tukked he was as is a frere aboute,</B><BR>
622	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And evere he rood the hyndreste of oure route.</B><BR>
623	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A SOMONOUR was ther with us in that place,</B><BR>
624	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That hadde a fyr-reed cherubynnes face,</B><BR>
625	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For saucefleem he was, with eyen narwe.</B><BR>
626	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>As hoot he was and lecherous as a sparwe,</B><BR>
627	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With scalled browes blake and piled berd.</B><BR>
628	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of his visage children were aferd.</B><BR>
629	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ther nas quyk-silver, lytarge, ne brymstoon,</B><BR>
630	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Boras, ceruce, ne oille of tartre noon,</B><BR>
631	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ne oynement that wolde clense and byte,</B><BR>
632	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That hym myghte helpen of his whelkes white,</B><BR>
633	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Nor of the knobbes sittynge on his chekes.</B><BR>
634	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel loved he garleek, oynons, and eek lekes,</B><BR>
635	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And for to drynken strong wyn, reed as blood;</B><BR>
636	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Thanne wolde he speke and crie as he were wood.</B><BR>
637	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And whan that he wel dronken hadde the wyn,</B><BR>
638	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Thanne wolde he speke no word but Latyn.</B><BR>
639	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A fewe termes hadde he, two or thre,</B><BR>
640	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That he had lerned out of som decree --</B><BR>
641	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>No wonder is, he herde it al the day;</B><BR>
642	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And eek ye knowen wel how that a jay</B><BR>
643	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Kan clepen "Watte" as wel as kan the pope.</B><BR>
644	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But whoso koude in oother thyng hym grope,</B><BR>
645	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Thanne hadde he spent al his philosophie;</B><BR>
646	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ay "Questio quid iuris" wolde he crie.</B><BR>
647	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was a gentil harlot and a kynde;</B><BR>
648	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A bettre felawe sholde men noght fynde.</B><BR>
649	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He wolde suffre for a quart of wyn</B><BR>
650	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A good felawe to have his concubyn</B><BR>
651	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A twelf month, and excuse hym atte fulle;</B><BR>
652	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful prively a fynch eek koude he pulle.</B><BR>
653	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And if he foond owher a good felawe,</B><BR>
654	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He wolde techen him to have noon awe</B><BR>
655	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In swich caas of the ercedekenes curs,</B><BR>
656	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But if a mannes soule were in his purs;</B><BR>
657	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For in his purs he sholde ypunysshed be.</B><BR>
658	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>"Purs is the ercedekenes helle," seyde he.</B><BR>
659	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But wel I woot he lyed right in dede;</B><BR>
660	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of cursyng oghte ech gilty man him drede,</B><BR>
661	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For curs wol slee right as assoillyng savith,</B><BR>
662	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And also war hym of a Significavit.</B><BR>
663	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In daunger hadde he at his owene gise</B><BR>
664	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The yonge girles of the diocise,</B><BR>
665	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And knew hir conseil, and was al hir reed.</B><BR>
666	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A gerland hadde he set upon his heed,</B><BR>
667	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>As greet as it were for an ale-stake.</B><BR>
668	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A bokeleer hadde he maad hym of a cake.</B><BR>
669	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With hym ther rood a gentil PARDONER</B><BR>
670	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of Rouncivale, his freend and his compeer,</B><BR>
671	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That streight was comen fro the court of Rome.</B><BR>
672	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ful loude he soong "Com hider, love, to me!"</B><BR>
673	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>This Somonour bar to hym a stif burdoun;</B><BR>
674	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Was nevere trompe of half so greet a soun.</B><BR>
675	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>This Pardoner hadde heer as yelow as wex,</B><BR>
676	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But smothe it heeng as dooth a strike of flex;</B><BR>
677	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>By ounces henge his lokkes that he hadde,</B><BR>
678	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And therwith he his shuldres overspradde;</B><BR>
679	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But thynne it lay, by colpons oon and oon.</B><BR>
680	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But hood, for jolitee, wered he noon,</B><BR>
681	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For it was trussed up in his walet.</B><BR>
682	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hym thoughte he rood al of the newe jet;</B><BR>
683	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Dischevelee, save his cappe, he rood al bare.</B><BR>
684	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Swiche glarynge eyen hadde he as an hare.</B><BR>
685	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A vernycle hadde he sowed upon his cappe.</B><BR>
686	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His walet, biforn hym in his lappe,</B><BR>
687	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Bretful of pardoun comen from Rome al hoot.</B><BR>
688	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A voys he hadde as smal as hath a goot.</B><BR>
689	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>No berd hadde he, ne nevere sholde have;</B><BR>
690	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>As smothe it was as it were late shave.</B><BR>
691	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>I trowe he were a geldyng or a mare.</B><BR>
692	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But of his craft, fro Berwyk into Ware</B><BR>
693	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ne was ther swich another pardoner.</B><BR>
694	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For in his male he hadde a pilwe-beer,</B><BR>
695	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Which that he seyde was Oure Lady veyl;</B><BR>
696	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He seyde he hadde a gobet of the seyl</B><BR>
697	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That Seint Peter hadde, whan that he wente</B><BR>
698	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Upon the see, til Jhesu Crist hym hente.</B><BR>
699	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He hadde a croys of latoun ful of stones,</B><BR>
700	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And in a glas he hadde pigges bones.</B><BR>
701	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But with thise relikes, whan that he fond</B><BR>
702	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A povre person dwellynge upon lond,</B><BR>
703	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Upon a day he gat hym moore moneye</B><BR>
704	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Than that the person gat in monthes tweye;</B><BR>
705	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And thus, with feyned flaterye and japes,</B><BR>
706	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He made the person and the peple his apes.</B><BR>
707	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But trewely to tellen atte laste,</B><BR>
708	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He was in chirche a noble ecclesiaste.</B><BR>
709	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Wel koude he rede a lessoun or a storie,</B><BR>
710	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But alderbest he song an offertorie;</B><BR>
711	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For wel he wiste, whan that song was songe,</B><BR>
712	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He moste preche and wel affile his tonge</B><BR>
713	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To wynne silver, as he ful wel koude;</B><BR>
714	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Therefore he song the murierly and loude.</B><BR>
715	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Now have I toold you soothly, in a clause,</B><BR>
716	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Th' estaat, th' array, the nombre, and eek the cause</B><BR>
717	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Why that assembled was this compaignye</B><BR>
718	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In Southwerk at this gentil hostelrye</B><BR>
719	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That highte the Tabard, faste by the Belle.</B><BR>
720	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But now is tyme to yow for to telle</B><BR>
721	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>How that we baren us that ilke nyght,</B><BR>
722	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Whan we were in that hostelrie alyght;</B><BR>
723	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And after wol I telle of our viage</B><BR>
724	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And al the remenaunt of oure pilgrimage.</B><BR>
725	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But first I pray yow, of youre curteisye,</B><BR>
726	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That ye n' arette it nat my vileynye,</B><BR>
727	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Thogh that I pleynly speke in this mateere,</B><BR>
728	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To telle yow hir wordes and hir cheere,</B><BR>
729	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ne thogh I speke hir wordes proprely.</B><BR>
730	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For this ye knowen al so wel as I:</B><BR>
731	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Whoso shal telle a tale after a man,</B><BR>
732	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He moot reherce as ny as evere he kan</B><BR>
733	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Everich a word, if it be in his charge,</B><BR>
734	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Al speke he never so rudeliche and large,</B><BR>
735	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Or ellis he moot telle his tale untrewe,</B><BR>
736	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Or feyne thyng, or fynde wordes newe.</B><BR>
737	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He may nat spare, althogh he were his brother;</B><BR>
738	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He moot as wel seye o word as another.</B><BR>
739	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Crist spak hymself ful brode in hooly writ,</B><BR>
740	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And wel ye woot no vileynye is it.</B><BR>
741	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Eek Plato seith, whoso kan hym rede,</B><BR>
742	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The wordes moote be cosyn to the dede.</B><BR>
743	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Also I prey yow to foryeve it me,</B><BR>
744	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Al have I nat set folk in hir degree</B><BR>
745	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Heere in this tale, as that they sholde stonde.</B><BR>
746	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>My wit is short, ye may wel understonde.</B><BR>
747	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Greet chiere made oure Hoost us everichon,</B><BR>
748	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And to the soper sette he us anon.</B><BR>
749	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He served us with vitaille at the beste;</B><BR>
750	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Strong was the wyn, and wel to drynke us leste.</B><BR>
751	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A semely man OURE HOOSTE was withalle</B><BR>
752	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For to been a marchal in an halle.</B><BR>
753	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A large man he was with eyen stepe --</B><BR>
754	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>A fairer burgeys was ther noon in Chepe --</B><BR>
755	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Boold of his speche, and wys, and wel ytaught,</B><BR>
756	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And of manhod hym lakkede right naught.</B><BR>
757	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Eek therto he was right a myrie man;</B><BR>
758	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And after soper pleyen he bigan,</B><BR>
759	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And spak of myrthe amonges othere thynges,</B><BR>
760	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Whan that we hadde maad oure rekenynges,</B><BR>
761	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And seyde thus: "Now, lordynges, trewely,</B><BR>
762	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ye been to me right welcome, hertely;</B><BR>
763	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For by my trouthe, if that I shal nat lye,</B><BR>
764	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>I saugh nat this yeer so myrie a compaignye</B><BR>
765	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Atones in this herberwe as is now.</B><BR>
766	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Fayn wolde I doon yow myrthe, wiste I how.</B><BR>
767	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And of a myrthe I am right now bythoght,</B><BR>
768	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To doon yow ese, and it shal coste noght.</B><BR>
769	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>"Ye goon to Caunterbury -- God yow speede,</B><BR>
770	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The blisful martir quite yow youre meede!</B><BR>
771	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And wel I woot, as ye goon by the weye,</B><BR>
772	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ye shapen yow to talen and to pleye;</B><BR>
773	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For trewely, confort ne myrthe is noon</B><BR>
774	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To ride by the weye doumb as a stoon;</B><BR>
775	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And therfore wol I maken yow disport,</B><BR>
776	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>As I seyde erst, and doon yow som confort.</B><BR>
777	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And if yow liketh alle by oon assent</B><BR>
778	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>For to stonden at my juggement,</B><BR>
779	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And for to werken as I shal yow seye,</B><BR>
780	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Tomorwe, whan ye riden by the weye,</B><BR>
781	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Now, by my fader soule that is deed,</B><BR>
782	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But ye be myrie, I wol yeve yow myn heed!</B><BR>
783	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Hoold up youre hondes, withouten moore speche."</B><BR>
784	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Oure conseil was nat longe for to seche.</B><BR>
785	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Us thoughte it was noght worth to make it wys,</B><BR>
786	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And graunted hym withouten moore avys,</B><BR>
787	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And bad him seye his voirdit as hym leste.</B><BR>
788	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>"Lordynges," quod he, "now herkneth for the beste;</B><BR>
789	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But taak it nought, I prey yow, in desdeyn.</B><BR>
790	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>This is the poynt, to speken short and pleyn,</B><BR>
791	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That ech of yow, to shorte with oure weye,</B><BR>
792	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In this viage shal telle tales tweye</B><BR>
793	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To Caunterbury-ward, I mene it so,</B><BR>
794	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And homward he shal tellen othere two,</B><BR>
795	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of aventures that whilom han bifalle.</B><BR>
796	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And which of yow that bereth hym best of alle --</B><BR>
797	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That is to seyn, that telleth in this caas</B><BR>
798	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Tales of best sentence and moost solaas --</B><BR>
799	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Shal have a soper at oure aller cost</B><BR>
800	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Heere in this place, sittynge by this post,</B><BR>
801	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Whan that we come agayn fro Caunterbury.</B><BR>
802	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And for to make yow the moore mury,</B><BR>
803	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>I wol myselven goodly with yow ryde,</B><BR>
804	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Right at myn owene cost, and be youre gyde;</B><BR>
805	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And whoso wole my juggement withseye</B><BR>
806	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Shal paye al that we spenden by the weye.</B><BR>
807	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And if ye vouche sauf that it be so,</B><BR>
808	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Tel me anon, withouten wordes mo,</B><BR>
809	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And I wol erly shape me therfore."</B><BR>
810	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>This thyng was graunted, and oure othes swore</B><BR>
811	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>With ful glad herte, and preyden hym also</B><BR>
812	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>That he wolde vouche sauf for to do so,</B><BR>
813	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And that he wolde been oure governour,</B><BR>
814	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And of oure tales juge and reportour,</B><BR>
815	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And sette a soper at a certeyn pris,</B><BR>
816	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And we wol reuled been at his devys</B><BR>
817	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>In heigh and lough; and thus by oon assent</B><BR>
818	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>We been acorded to his juggement.</B><BR>
819	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And therupon the wyn was fet anon;</B><BR>
820	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>We dronken, and to reste wente echon,</B><BR>
821	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Withouten any lenger taryynge.</B><BR>
822	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Amorwe, whan that day bigan to sprynge,</B><BR>
823	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Up roos oure Hoost, and was oure aller cok,</B><BR>
824	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And gadrede us togidre alle in a flok,</B><BR>
825	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And forth we riden a litel moore than paas</B><BR>
826	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Unto the Wateryng of Seint Thomas;</B><BR>
827	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And there oure Hoost bigan his hors areste</B><BR>
828	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And seyde, "Lordynges, herkneth, if yow leste.</B><BR>
829	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ye woot youre foreward, and I it yow recorde.</B><BR>
830	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>If even-song and morwe-song accorde,</B><BR>
831	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Lat se now who shal telle the firste tale.</B><BR>
832	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>As evere mote I drynke wyn or ale,</B><BR>
833	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Whoso be rebel to my juggement</B><BR>
834	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Shal paye for al that by the wey is spent.</B><BR>
835	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Now draweth cut, er that we ferrer twynne;</B><BR>
836	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He which that hath the shorteste shal bigynne.</B><BR>
837	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Sire Knyght," quod he, "my mayster and my lord,</B><BR>
838	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Now draweth cut, for that is myn accord.</B><BR>
839	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Cometh neer," quod he, "my lady Prioresse.</B><BR>
840	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And ye, sire Clerk, lat be youre shamefastnesse,</B><BR>
841	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Ne studieth noght; ley hond to, every man!"</B><BR>
842	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Anon to drawen every wight bigan,</B><BR>
843	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And shortly for to tellen as it was,</B><BR>
844	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Were it by aventure, or sort, or cas,</B><BR>
845	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>The sothe is this: the cut fil to the Knyght,</B><BR>
846	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Of which ful blithe and glad was every wyght,</B><BR>
847	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And telle he moste his tale, as was resoun,</B><BR>
848	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>By foreward and by composicioun,</B><BR>
849	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>As ye han herd; what nedeth wordes mo?</B><BR>
850	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And whan this goode man saugh that it was so,</B><BR>
851	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>As he that wys was and obedient</B><BR>
852	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>To kepe his foreward by his free assent,</B><BR>
853	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>He seyde, "Syn I shal bigynne the game,</B><BR>
854	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>What, welcome be the cut, a Goddes name!</B><BR>
855	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Now lat us ryde, and herkneth what I seye."</B><BR>
856	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And with that word we ryden forth oure weye,</B><BR>
857	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>And he bigan with right a myrie cheere</B><BR>
858	&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>His tale anon, and seyde as ye may heere.</B><BR>
1355 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan that Arcite to Thebes comen was,</B><BR>
1356 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful ofte a day he swelte and seyde "Allas!"</B><BR>
1357 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For seen his lady shal he nevere mo.</B><BR>
1358 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And shortly to concluden al his wo,</B><BR>
1359 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So muche sorwe hadde nevere creature</B><BR>
1360 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That is, or shal, whil that the world may dure.</B><BR>
1361 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His slep, his mete, his drynke, is hym biraft,</B><BR>
1362 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That lene he wex and drye as is a shaft;</B><BR>
1363 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His eyen holwe and grisly to biholde,</B><BR>
1364 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His hewe falow and pale as asshen colde,</B><BR>
1365 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And solitarie he was and evere allone,</B><BR>
1366 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And waillynge al the nyght, makynge his mone;</B><BR>
1367 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And if he herde song or instrument,</B><BR>
1368 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne wolde he wepe, he myghte nat be stent.</B><BR>
1369 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So feble eek were his spiritz, and so lowe,</B><BR>
1370 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And chaunged so, that no man koude knowe</B><BR>
1371 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His speche nor his voys, though men it herde.</B><BR>
1372 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in his geere for al the world he ferde</B><BR>
1373 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Nat oonly lik the loveris maladye</B><BR>
1374 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of Hereos, but rather lyk manye,</B><BR>
1375 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Engendred of humour malencolik</B><BR>
1376 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Biforen, in his celle fantastik.</B><BR>
1377 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And shortly, turned was al up so doun</B><BR>
1378 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bothe habit and eek disposicioun</B><BR>
1379 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of hym, this woful lovere daun Arcite.</B><BR>
1380 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>What sholde I al day of his wo endite?</B><BR>
1381 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan he endured hadde a yeer or two</B><BR>
1382 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This crueel torment and this peyne and wo,</B><BR>
1383 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>At Thebes, in his contree, as I seyde,</B><BR>
1384 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon a nyght in sleep as he hym leyde,</B><BR>
1385 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hym thoughte how that the wynged god Mercurie</B><BR>
1386 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Biforn hym stood and bad hym to be murie.</B><BR>
1387 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His slepy yerde in hond he bar uprighte;</B><BR>
1388 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>An hat he werede upon his heris brighte.</B><BR>
1389 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Arrayed was this god, as he took keep,</B><BR>
1390 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As he was whan that Argus took his sleep;</B><BR>
1391 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And seyde hym thus: "To Atthenes shaltou wende,</B><BR>
1392 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther is thee shapen of thy wo an ende."</B><BR>
1393 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with that word Arcite wook and sterte.</B><BR>
1394 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Now trewely, hou soore that me smerte,"</B><BR>
1395 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Quod he, "to Atthenes right now wol I fare,</B><BR>
1396 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne for the drede of deeth shal I nat spare</B><BR>
1397 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To se my lady, that I love and serve.</B><BR>
1398 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In hire presence I recche nat to sterve."</B><BR>
1399 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with that word he caughte a greet mirour,</B><BR>
1400 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And saugh that chaunged was al his colour,</B><BR>
1401 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And saugh his visage al in another kynde.</B><BR>
1402 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And right anon it ran hym in his mynde,</B><BR>
1403 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That, sith his face was so disfigured</B><BR>
1404 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of maladye the which he hadde endured,</B><BR>
1405 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He myghte wel, if that he bar hym lowe,</B><BR>
1406 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lyve in Atthenes everemoore unknowe,</B><BR>
1407 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And seen his lady wel ny day by day.</B><BR>
1408 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And right anon he chaunged his array,</B><BR>
1409 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And cladde hym as a povre laborer,</B><BR>
1410 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And al allone, save oonly a squier</B><BR>
1411 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That knew his privetee and al his cas,</B><BR>
1412 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Which was disgised povrely as he was,</B><BR>
1413 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To Atthenes is he goon the nexte way.</B><BR>
1414 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And to the court he wente upon a day,</B><BR>
1415 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And at the gate he profreth his servyse</B><BR>
1416 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To drugge and drawe, what so men wol devyse.</B><BR>
1417 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And shortly of this matere for to seyn,</B><BR>
1418 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He fil in office with a chamberleyn</B><BR>
1419 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The which that dwellynge was with Emelye,</B><BR>
1420 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For he was wys and koude soone espye,</B><BR>
1421 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of every servaunt, which that serveth here.</B><BR>
1422 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wel koude he hewen wode, and water bere,</B><BR>
1423 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For he was yong and myghty for the nones,</B><BR>
1424 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And therto he was long and big of bones</B><BR>
1425 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To doon that any wight kan hym devyse.</B><BR>
1426 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A yeer or two he was in this servyse,</B><BR>
1427 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Page of the chambre of Emelye the brighte,</B><BR>
1428 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Philostrate he seyde that he highte.</B><BR>
1429 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But half so wel biloved a man as he</B><BR>
1430 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne was ther nevere in court of his degree;</B><BR>
1431 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He was so gentil of condicioun</B><BR>
1432 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That thurghout al the court was his renoun.</B><BR>
1433 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>They seyden that it were a charitee</B><BR>
1434 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That Theseus wolde enhauncen his degree,</B><BR>
1435 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And putten hym in worshipful servyse,</B><BR>
1436 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther as he myghte his vertu excercise.</B><BR>
1437 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thus withinne a while his name is spronge,</B><BR>
1438 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bothe of his dedes and his goode tonge,</B><BR>
1439 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That Theseus hath taken hym so neer</B><BR>
1440 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That of his chambre he made hym a squier,</B><BR>
1441 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And gaf hym gold to mayntene his degree.</B><BR>
1442 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek men broghte hym out of his contree,</B><BR>
1443 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>From yeer to yeer, ful pryvely his rente;</B><BR>
1444 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But honestly and slyly he it spente,</B><BR>
1445 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That no man wondred how that he it hadde.</B><BR>
1446 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thre yeer in this wise his lif he ladde,</B><BR>
1447 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And bar hym so, in pees and eek in werre,</B><BR>
1448 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther was no man that Theseus hath derre.</B><BR>
1449 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in this blisse lete I now Arcite,</B><BR>
1450 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And speke I wole of Palamon a lite.</B><BR>
1451 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In derknesse and horrible and strong prisoun</B><BR>
1452 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thise seven yeer hath seten Palamoun</B><BR>
1453 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Forpyned, what for wo and for distresse.</B><BR>
1454 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Who feeleth double soor and hevynesse</B><BR>
1455 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But Palamon, that love destreyneth so</B><BR>
1456 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That wood out of his wit he goth for wo?</B><BR>
1457 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek therto he is a prisoner</B><BR>
1458 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Perpetuelly, noght oonly for a yer.</B><BR>
1459 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Who koude ryme in Englyssh proprely</B><BR>
1460 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His martirdom? For sothe it am nat I;</B><BR>
1461 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Therfore I passe as lightly as I may.</B><BR>
1462 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>It fel that in the seventhe yer, of May</B><BR>
1463 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The thridde nyght (as olde bookes seyn,</B><BR>
1464 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That al this storie tellen moore pleyn),</B><BR>
1465 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Were it by aventure or destynee --</B><BR>
1466 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As, whan a thyng is shapen, it shal be --</B><BR>
1467 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That soone after the mydnyght Palamoun,</B><BR>
1468 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>By helpyng of a freend, brak his prisoun</B><BR>
1469 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And fleeth the citee faste as he may go.</B><BR>
1470 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For he hadde yeve his gayler drynke so</B><BR>
1471 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of a clarree maad of a certeyn wyn,</B><BR>
1472 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With nercotikes and opie of Thebes fyn,</B><BR>
1473 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That al that nyght, thogh that men wolde him shake,</B><BR>
1474 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The gayler sleep; he myghte nat awake.</B><BR>
1475 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thus he fleeth as faste as evere he may.</B><BR>
1476 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The nyght was short and faste by the day</B><BR>
1477 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That nedes cost he moot hymselven hyde,</B><BR>
1478 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And til a grove faste ther bisyde</B><BR>
1479 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With dredeful foot thanne stalketh Palamon.</B><BR>
1480 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For, shortly, this was his opinion:</B><BR>
1481 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That in that grove he wolde hym hyde al day,</B><BR>
1482 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in the nyght thanne wolde he take his way</B><BR>
1483 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To Thebes-ward, his freendes for to preye</B><BR>
1484 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>On Theseus to helpe him to werreye;</B><BR>
1485 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And shortly, outher he wolde lese his lif</B><BR>
1486 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Or wynnen Emelye unto his wyf.</B><BR>
1487 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This is th'effect and his entente pleyn.</B><BR>
1488 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now wol I turne to Arcite ageyn,</B><BR>
1489 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That litel wiste how ny that was his care,</B><BR>
1490 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Til that Fortune had broght him in the snare.</B><BR>
1491 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The bisy larke, messager of day,</B><BR>
1492 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Salueth in hir song the morwe gray,</B><BR>
1493 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And firy Phebus riseth up so bright</B><BR>
1494 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That al the orient laugheth of the light,</B><BR>
1495 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with his stremes dryeth in the greves</B><BR>
1496 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The silver dropes hangynge on the leves.</B><BR>
1497 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Arcita, that in the court roial</B><BR>
1498 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With Theseus is principal squier,</B><BR>
1499 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Is risen and looketh on the myrie day.</B><BR>
1500 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And for to doon his observaunce to May,</B><BR>
1501 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Remembrynge on the poynt of his desir,</B><BR>
1502 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He on a courser, startlynge as the fir,</B><BR>
1503 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Is riden into the feeldes hym to pleye,</B><BR>
1504 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Out of the court, were it a myle or tweye.</B><BR>
1505 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And to the grove of which that I yow tolde</B><BR>
1506 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>By aventure his wey he gan to holde</B><BR>
1507 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To maken hym a gerland of the greves,</B><BR>
1508 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Were it of wodebynde or hawethorn leves,</B><BR>
1509 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And loude he song ayeyn the sonne shene:</B><BR>
1510 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"May, with alle thy floures and thy grene,</B><BR>
1511 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Welcome be thou, faire, fresshe May,</B><BR>
1512 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In hope that I som grene gete may."</B><BR>
1513 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And from his courser, with a lusty herte,</B><BR>
1514 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Into the grove ful hastily he sterte,</B><BR>
1515 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in a path he rometh up and doun,</B><BR>
1516 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther as by aventure this Palamoun</B><BR>
1517 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Was in a bussh, that no man myghte hym se,</B><BR>
1518 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For soore afered of his deeth was he.</B><BR>
1519 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>No thyng ne knew he that it was Arcite;</B><BR>
1520 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>God woot he wolde have trowed it ful lite.</B><BR>
1521 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But sooth is seyd, go sithen many yeres,</B><BR>
1522 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That "feeld hath eyen and the wode hath eres."</B><BR>
1523 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>It is ful fair a man to bere hym evene,</B><BR>
1524 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For al day meeteth men at unset stevene.</B><BR>
1525 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful litel woot Arcite of his felawe,</B><BR>
1526 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That was so ny to herknen al his sawe,</B><BR>
1527 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For in the bussh he sitteth now ful stille.</B><BR>
1528 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan that Arcite hadde romed al his fille,</B><BR>
1529 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And songen al the roundel lustily,</B><BR>
1530 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Into a studie he fil sodeynly,</B><BR>
1531 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As doon thise loveres in hir queynte geres,</B><BR>
1532 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now in the crope, now doun in the breres,</B><BR>
1533 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now up, now doun, as boket in a welle.</B><BR>
1534 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Right as the Friday, soothly for to telle,</B><BR>
1535 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now it shyneth, now it reyneth faste,</B><BR>
1536 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Right so kan geery Venus overcaste</B><BR>
1537 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The hertes of hir folk; right as hir day</B><BR>
1538 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Is gereful, right so chaungeth she array.</B><BR>
1539 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Selde is the Friday al the wowke ylike.</B><BR>
1540 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan that Arcite had songe, he gan to sike</B><BR>
1541 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And sette hym doun withouten any moore.</B><BR>
1542 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Allas," quod he, "that day that I was bore!</B><BR>
1543 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>How longe, Juno, thurgh thy crueltee,</B><BR>
1544 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Woltow werreyen Thebes the citee?</B><BR>
1545 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Allas, ybroght is to confusioun</B><BR>
1546 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The blood roial of Cadme and Amphioun --</B><BR>
1547 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of Cadmus, which that was the firste man</B><BR>
1548 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That Thebes bulte, or first the toun bigan,</B><BR>
1549 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And of the citee first was crouned kyng.</B><BR>
1550 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of his lynage am I and his ofspryng</B><BR>
1551 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>By verray ligne, as of the stok roial,</B><BR>
1552 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And now I am so caytyf and so thral,</B><BR>
1553 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That he that is my mortal enemy,</B><BR>
1554 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I serve hym as his squier povrely.</B><BR>
1555 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And yet dooth Juno me wel moore shame,</B><BR>
1556 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For I dar noght biknowe myn owene name;</B><BR>
1557 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But ther as I was wont to highte Arcite,</B><BR>
1558 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now highte I Philostrate, noght worth a myte.</B><BR>
1559 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Allas, thou felle Mars! Allas, Juno!</B><BR>
1560 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thus hath youre ire oure lynage al fordo,</B><BR>
1561 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Save oonly me and wrecched Palamoun,</B><BR>
1562 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That Theseus martireth in prisoun.</B><BR>
1563 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And over al this, to sleen me outrely</B><BR>
1564 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Love hath his firy dart so brennyngly</B><BR>
1565 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ystiked thurgh my trewe, careful herte</B><BR>
1566 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That shapen was my deeth erst than my sherte.</B><BR>
1567 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ye sleen me with youre eyen, Emelye!</B><BR>
1568 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ye been the cause wherfore that I dye.</B><BR>
1569 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of al the remenant of myn oother care</B><BR>
1570 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne sette I nat the montance of a tare,</B><BR>
1571 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So that I koude doon aught to youre plesaunce."</B><BR>
1572 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with that word he fil doun in a traunce</B><BR>
1573 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A longe tyme, and after he up sterte.</B><BR>
1574 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This Palamoun, that thoughte that thurgh his herte</B><BR>
1575 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He felte a coold swerd sodeynliche glyde,</B><BR>
1576 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For ire he quook; no lenger wolde he byde.</B><BR>
1577 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And whan that he had herd Arcites tale,</B><BR>
1578 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As he were wood, with face deed and pale,</B><BR>
1579 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He stirte hym up out of the buskes thikke</B><BR>
1580 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And seide: "Arcite, false traytour wikke,</B><BR>
1581 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now artow hent, that lovest my lady so,</B><BR>
1582 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For whom that I have al this peyne and wo,</B><BR>
1583 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And art my blood, and to my conseil sworn,</B><BR>
1584 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As I ful ofte have told thee heerbiforn,</B><BR>
1585 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And hast byjaped heere duc Theseus,</B><BR>
1586 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And falsly chaunged hast thy name thus!</B><BR>
1587 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I wol be deed, or elles thou shalt dye.</B><BR>
1588 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thou shalt nat love my lady Emelye,</B><BR>
1589 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But I wol love hire oonly and namo;</B><BR>
1590 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For I am Palamon, thy mortal foo.</B><BR>
1591 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And though that I no wepene have in this place,</B><BR>
1592 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But out of prison am astert by grace,</B><BR>
1593 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I drede noght that outher thow shalt dye,</B><BR>
1594 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Or thow ne shalt nat loven Emelye.</B><BR>
1595 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Chees which thou wolt, or thou shalt nat asterte!"</B><BR>
1596 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This Arcite, with ful despitous herte,</B><BR>
1597 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan he hym knew, and hadde his tale herd,</B><BR>
1598 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As fiers as leon pulled out his swerd,</B><BR>
1599 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And seyde thus: "By God that sit above,</B><BR>
1600 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Nere it that thou art sik and wood for love,</B><BR>
1601 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek that thow no wepne hast in this place,</B><BR>
1602 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thou sholdest nevere out of this grove pace,</B><BR>
1603 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That thou ne sholdest dyen of myn hond.</B><BR>
1604 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For I defye the seurete and the bond</B><BR>
1605 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Which that thou seist that I have maad to thee.</B><BR>
1606 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>What! Verray fool, thynk wel that love is free,</B><BR>
1607 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And I wol love hire maugree al thy myght!</B><BR>
1608 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But for as muche thou art a worthy knyght</B><BR>
1609 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And wilnest to darreyne hire by bataille,</B><BR>
1610 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Have heer my trouthe; tomorwe I wol nat faille,</B><BR>
1611 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Withoute wityng of any oother wight,</B><BR>
1612 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That heere I wol be founden as a knyght,</B><BR>
1613 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And bryngen harneys right ynough for thee;</B><BR>
1614 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And ches the beste, and leef the worste for me.</B><BR>
1615 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And mete and drynke this nyght wol I brynge</B><BR>
1616 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ynough for thee, and clothes for thy beddynge.</B><BR>
1617 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And if so be that thou my lady wynne,</B><BR>
1618 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And sle me in this wode ther I am inne,</B><BR>
1619 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thow mayst wel have thy lady as for me."</B><BR>
1620 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This Palamon answerde, "I graunte it thee."</B><BR>
1621 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thus they been departed til amorwe, </B><BR>
1622 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan ech of hem had leyd his feith to borwe.</B><BR>
1623 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>O Cupide, out of alle charitee!</B><BR>
1624 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>O regne, that wolt no felawe have with thee!</B><BR>
1625 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful sooth is seyd that love ne lordshipe</B><BR>
1626 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wol noght, his thankes, have no felaweshipe.</B><BR>
1627 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wel fynden that Arcite and Palamoun.</B><BR>
1628 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Arcite is riden anon unto the toun,</B><BR>
1629 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And on the morwe, er it were dayes light,</B><BR>
1630 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful prively two harneys hath he dight,</B><BR>
1631 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bothe suffisaunt and mete to darreyne</B><BR>
1632 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The bataille in the feeld bitwix hem tweyne;</B><BR>
1633 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And on his hors, allone as he was born,</B><BR>
1634 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He carieth al the harneys hym biforn.</B><BR>
1635 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in the grove, at tyme and place yset,</B><BR>
1636 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This Arcite and this Palamon ben met.</B><BR>
1637 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To chaungen gan the colour in hir face;</B><BR>
1638 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Right as the hunters in the regne of Trace,</B><BR>
1639 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That stondeth at the gappe with a spere,</B><BR>
1640 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan hunted is the leon or the bere,</B><BR>
1641 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And hereth hym come russhyng in the greves,</B><BR>
1642 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And breketh bothe bowes and the leves,</B><BR>
1643 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thynketh, "Heere cometh my mortal enemy!</B><BR>
1644 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Withoute faille, he moot be deed, or I,</B><BR>
1645 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For outher I moot sleen hym at the gappe,</B><BR>
1646 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Or he moot sleen me, if that me myshappe."</B><BR>
1647 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So ferden they in chaungyng of hir hewe,</B><BR>
1648 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As fer as everich of hem oother knewe.</B><BR>
1649 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther nas no good day, ne no saluyng,</B><BR>
1650 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But streight, withouten word or rehersyng,</B><BR>
1651 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Everich of hem heelp for to armen oother</B><BR>
1652 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As freendly as he were his owene brother;</B><BR>
1653 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And after that, with sharpe speres stronge</B><BR>
1654 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>They foynen ech at oother wonder longe.</B><BR>
1655 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thou myghtest wene that this Palamon</B><BR>
1656 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In his fightyng were a wood leon,</B><BR>
1657 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And as a crueel tigre was Arcite;</B><BR>
1658 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As wilde bores gonne they to smyte,</B><BR>
1659 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That frothen whit as foom for ire wood.</B><BR>
1660 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Up to the ancle foghte they in hir blood.</B><BR>
1661 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in this wise I lete hem fightyng dwelle,</B><BR>
1662 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And forth I wole of Theseus yow telle.</B><BR>
1663 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The destinee, ministre general,</B><BR>
1664 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That executeth in the world over al</B><BR>
1665 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The purveiaunce that God hath seyn biforn,</B><BR>
1666 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So strong it is that, though the world had sworn</B><BR>
1667 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The contrarie of a thyng by ye or nay,</B><BR>
1668 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yet somtyme it shal fallen on a day</B><BR>
1669 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That falleth nat eft withinne a thousand yeer.</B><BR>
1670 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For certeinly, oure appetites heer,</B><BR>
1671 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Be it of werre, or pees, or hate, or love,</B><BR>
1672 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al is this reuled by the sighte above.</B><BR>
1673 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This mene I now by myghty Theseus,</B><BR>
1674 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That for to hunten is so desirus,</B><BR>
1675 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And namely at the grete hert in May,</B><BR>
1676 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That in his bed ther daweth hym no day</B><BR>
1677 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That he nys clad, and redy for to ryde</B><BR>
1678 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With hunte and horn and houndes hym bisyde.</B><BR>
1679 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For in his huntyng hath he swich delit</B><BR>
1680 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That it is al his joye and appetit</B><BR>
1681 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To been hymself the grete hertes bane,</B><BR>
1682 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For after Mars he serveth now Dyane.</B><BR>
1683 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Cleer was the day, as I have toold er this,</B><BR>
1684 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Theseus with alle joye and blis,</B><BR>
1685 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With his Ypolita, the faire queene,</B><BR>
1686 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Emelye, clothed al in grene,</B><BR>
1687 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>On huntyng be they riden roially.</B><BR>
1688 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And to the grove that stood ful faste by,</B><BR>
1689 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In which ther was an hert, as men hym tolde,</B><BR>
1690 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Duc Theseus the streighte wey hath holde.</B><BR>
1691 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And to the launde he rideth hym ful right,</B><BR>
1692 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For thider was the hert wont have his flight,</B><BR>
1693 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And over a brook, and so forth on his weye.</B><BR>
1694 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This duc wol han a cours at hym or tweye</B><BR>
1695 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With houndes swiche as that hym list comaunde.</B><BR>
1696 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And whan this duc was come unto the launde,</B><BR>
1697 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Under the sonne he looketh, and anon</B><BR>
1698 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He was war of Arcite and Palamon,</B><BR>
1699 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That foughten breme as it were bores two.</B><BR>
1700 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The brighte swerdes wenten to and fro</B><BR>
1701 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So hidously that with the leeste strook</B><BR>
1702 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>It semed as it wolde felle an ook.</B><BR>
1703 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But what they were, no thyng he ne woot.</B><BR>
1704 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This duc his courser with his spores smoot,</B><BR>
1705 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And at a stert he was bitwix hem two,</B><BR>
1706 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And pulled out a swerd and cride, "Hoo!</B><BR>
1707 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Namoore, up peyne of lesynge of youre heed!</B><BR>
1708 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>By myghty Mars, he shal anon be deed</B><BR>
1709 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That smyteth any strook that I may seen.</B><BR>
1710 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But telleth me what myster men ye been,</B><BR>
1711 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That been so hardy for to fighten heere</B><BR>
1712 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Withouten juge or oother officere,</B><BR>
1713 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As it were in a lystes roially."</B><BR>
1714 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This Palamon answerde hastily</B><BR>
1715 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And seyde, "Sire, what nedeth wordes mo?</B><BR>
1716 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>We have the deeth disserved bothe two.</B><BR>
1717 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Two woful wrecches been we, two caytyves,</B><BR>
1718 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That been encombred of oure owene lyves;</B><BR>
1719 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And as thou art a rightful lord and juge,</B><BR>
1720 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne yif us neither mercy ne refuge,</B><BR>
1721 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But sle me first, for seinte charitee!</B><BR>
1722 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But sle my felawe eek as wel as me;</B><BR>
1723 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Or sle hym first, for though thow knowest it lite,</B><BR>
1724 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This is thy mortal foo, this is Arcite,</B><BR>
1725 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That fro thy lond is banysshed on his heed,</B><BR>
1726 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For which he hath deserved to be deed.</B><BR>
1727 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For this is he that cam unto thy gate</B><BR>
1728 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And seyde that he highte Philostrate.</B><BR>
1729 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thus hath he japed thee ful many a yer,</B><BR>
1730 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thou hast maked hym thy chief squier;</B><BR>
1731 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And this is he that loveth Emelye.</B><BR>
1732 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For sith the day is come that I shal dye,</B><BR>
1733 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I make pleynly my confessioun</B><BR>
1734 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That I am thilke woful Palamoun</B><BR>
1735 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That hath thy prisoun broken wikkedly.</B><BR>
1736 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I am thy mortal foo, and it am I</B><BR>
1737 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That loveth so hoote Emelye the brighte</B><BR>
1738 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That I wol dye present in hir sighte.</B><BR>
1739 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wherfore I axe deeth and my juwise;</B><BR>
1740 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But sle my felawe in the same wise,</B><BR>
1741 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For bothe han we deserved to be slayn."</B><BR>
1742 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This worthy duc answerde anon agayn,</B><BR>
1743 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And seyde, "This is a short conclusioun.</B><BR>
1744 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Youre owene mouth, by youre confessioun,</B><BR>
1745 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hath dampned yow, and I wol it recorde;</B><BR>
1746 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>It nedeth noght to pyne yow with the corde.</B><BR>
1747 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ye shal be deed, by myghty Mars the rede!"</B><BR>
1748 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The queene anon, for verray wommanhede,</B><BR>
1749 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Gan for to wepe, and so dide Emelye,</B><BR>
1750 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And alle the ladyes in the compaignye.</B><BR>
1751 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Greet pitee was it, as it thoughte hem alle,</B><BR>
1752 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That evere swich a chaunce sholde falle,</B><BR>
1753 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For gentil men they were of greet estaat,</B><BR>
1754 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And no thyng but for love was this debaat;</B><BR>
1755 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And saugh hir blody woundes wyde and soore,</B><BR>
1756 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And alle crieden, bothe lasse and moore,</B><BR>
1757 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Have mercy, Lord, upon us wommen alle!"</B><BR>
1758 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And on hir bare knees adoun they falle</B><BR>
1759 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And wolde have kist his feet ther as he stood;</B><BR>
1760 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Til at the laste aslaked was his mood,</B><BR>
1761 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For pitee renneth soone in gentil herte.</B><BR>
1762 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And though he first for ire quook and sterte,</B><BR>
1763 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He hath considered shortly, in a clause,</B><BR>
1764 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The trespas of hem bothe, and eek the cause,</B><BR>
1765 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And although that his ire hir gilt accused,</B><BR>
1766 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yet in his resoun he hem bothe excused,</B><BR>
1767 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As thus: he thoghte wel that every man</B><BR>
1768 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wol helpe hymself in love, if that he kan,</B><BR>
1769 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek delivere hymself out of prisoun.</B><BR>
1770 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek his herte hadde compassioun</B><BR>
1771 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of wommen, for they wepen evere in oon,</B><BR>
1772 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in his gentil herte he thoughte anon,</B><BR>
1773 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And softe unto hymself he seyde, "Fy</B><BR>
1774 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon a lord that wol have no mercy,</B><BR>
1775 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But been a leon, bothe in word and dede,</B><BR>
1776 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To hem that been in repentaunce and drede,</B><BR>
1777 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As wel as to a proud despitous man</B><BR>
1778 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That wol mayntene that he first bigan.</B><BR>
1779 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That lord hath litel of discrecioun,</B><BR>
1780 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That in swich cas kan no divisioun</B><BR>
1781 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But weyeth pride and humblesse after oon."</B><BR>
1782 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And shortly, whan his ire is thus agoon,</B><BR>
1783 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He gan to looken up with eyen lighte</B><BR>
1784 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And spak thise same wordes al on highte:</B><BR>
1785 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"The god of love, a benedicite!</B><BR>
1786 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>How myghty and how greet a lord is he!</B><BR>
1787 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ayeyns his myght ther gayneth none obstacles.</B><BR>
1788 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He may be cleped a god for his myracles,</B><BR>
1789 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For he kan maken, at his owene gyse,</B><BR>
1790 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of everich herte as that hym list divyse.</B><BR>
1791 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lo heere this Arcite and this Palamoun,</B><BR>
1792 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That quitly weren out of my prisoun,</B><BR>
1793 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And myghte han lyved in Thebes roially,</B><BR>
1794 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And witen I am hir mortal enemy,</B><BR>
1795 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And that hir deth lith in my myght also,</B><BR>
