1796 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And yet hath love, maugree hir eyen two,</B><BR>
1797 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Broght hem hyder bothe for to dye.</B><BR>
1798 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now looketh, is nat that an heigh folye?</B><BR>
1799 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Who may been a fool but if he love?</B><BR>
1800 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bihoold, for Goddes sake that sit above,</B><BR>
1801 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Se how they blede! Be they noght wel arrayed?</B><BR>
1802 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thus hath hir lord, the god of love, ypayed</B><BR>
1803 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hir wages and hir fees for hir servyse!</B><BR>
1804 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And yet they wenen for to been ful wyse</B><BR>
1805 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That serven love, for aught that may bifalle.</B><BR>
1806 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But this is yet the beste game of alle,</B><BR>
1807 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That she for whom they han this jolitee</B><BR>
1808 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Kan hem therfore as muche thank as me.</B><BR>
1809 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>She woot namoore of al this hoote fare,</B><BR>
1810 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>By God, than woot a cokkow or an hare!</B><BR>
1811 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But all moot ben assayed, hoot and coold;</B><BR>
1812 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A man moot ben a fool, or yong or oold --</B><BR>
1813 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I woot it by myself ful yore agon,</B><BR>
1814 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For in my tyme a servant was I oon.</B><BR>
1815 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And therfore, syn I knowe of loves peyne</B><BR>
1816 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And woot hou soore it kan a man distreyne,</B><BR>
1817 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As he that hath ben caught ofte in his laas,</B><BR>
1818 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I yow foryeve al hoolly this trespaas,</B><BR>
1819 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>At requeste of the queene, that kneleth heere,</B><BR>
1820 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek of Emelye, my suster deere.</B><BR>
1821 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And ye shul bothe anon unto me swere</B><BR>
1822 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That nevere mo ye shal my contree dere,</B><BR>
1823 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne make werre upon me nyght ne day,</B><BR>
1824 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But been my freendes in all that ye may.</B><BR>
1825 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I yow foryeve this trespas every deel."</B><BR>
1826 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And they hym sworen his axyng faire and weel,</B><BR>
1827 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And hym of lordshipe and of mercy preyde,</B><BR>
1828 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And he hem graunteth grace, and thus he seyde:</B><BR>
1829 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"To speke of roial lynage and richesse,</B><BR>
1830 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Though that she were a queene or a princesse,</B><BR>
1831 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ech of you bothe is worthy, doutelees,</B><BR>
1832 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To wedden whan tyme is; but nathelees --</B><BR>
1833 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I speke as for my suster Emelye,</B><BR>
1834 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For whom ye have this strif and jalousye --</B><BR>
1835 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ye woot yourself she may nat wedden two</B><BR>
1836 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Atones, though ye fighten everemo,</B><BR>
1837 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That oon of you, al be hym looth or lief,</B><BR>
1838 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He moot go pipen in an yvy leef;</B><BR>
1839 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This is to seyn, she may nat now han bothe,</B><BR>
1840 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al be ye never so jalouse ne so wrothe.</B><BR>
1841 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And forthy I yow putte in this degree,</B><BR>
1842 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That ech of yow shal have his destynee</B><BR>
1843 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As hym is shape, and herkneth in what wyse;</B><BR>
1844 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lo, heere youre ende of that I shal devyse.</B><BR>
1845 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>My wyl is this, for plat conclusioun,</B><BR>
1846 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Withouten any repplicacioun --</B><BR>
1847 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>If that you liketh, take it for the beste:</B><BR>
1848 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That everich of you shal goon where hym leste</B><BR>
1849 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Frely, withouten raunson or daunger,</B><BR>
1850 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And this day fifty wykes, fer ne ner,</B><BR>
1851 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Everich of you shal brynge an hundred knyghtes</B><BR>
1852 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Armed for lystes up at alle rightes,</B><BR>
1853 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al redy to darreyne hire by bataille.</B><BR>
1854 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And this bihote I yow withouten faille,</B><BR>
1855 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon my trouthe, and as I am a knyght,</B><BR>
1856 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That wheither of yow bothe that hath myght --</B><BR>
1857 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This is to seyn, that wheither he or thow</B><BR>
1858 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>May with his hundred, as I spak of now,</B><BR>
1859 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Sleen his contrarie, or out of lystes dryve,</B><BR>
1860 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne shal I yeve Emelya to wyve</B><BR>
1861 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To whom that Fortune yeveth so fair a grace.</B><BR>
1862 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The lystes shal I maken in this place,</B><BR>
1863 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And God so wisly on my soule rewe</B><BR>
1864 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As I shal evene juge been and trewe.</B><BR>
1865 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ye shul noon oother ende with me maken,</B><BR>
1866 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That oon of yow ne shal be deed or taken.</B><BR>
1867 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And if yow thynketh this is weel ysayd,</B><BR>
1868 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Seyeth youre avys, and holdeth you apayd.</B><BR>
1869 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This is youre ende and youre conclusioun."</B><BR>
1870 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Who looketh lightly now but Palamoun?</B><BR>
1871 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Who spryngeth up for joye but Arcite?</B><BR>
1872 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Who kouthe telle, or who kouthe it endite,</B><BR>
1873 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The joye that is maked in the place</B><BR>
1874 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan Theseus hath doon so fair a grace?</B><BR>
1875 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But doun on knees wente every maner wight,</B><BR>
1876 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thonked hym with al hir herte and myght,</B><BR>
1877 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And namely the Thebans often sithe.</B><BR>
1878 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thus with good hope and with herte blithe</B><BR>
1879 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>They taken hir leve, and homward gonne they ride</B><BR>
1880 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To Thebes with his olde walles wyde.</B><BR>
1881 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I trowe men wolde deme it necligence</B><BR>
1882 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>If I foryete to tellen the dispence</B><BR>
1883 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of Theseus, that gooth so bisily</B><BR>
1884 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To maken up the lystes roially,</B><BR>
1885 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That swich a noble theatre as it was</B><BR>
1886 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I dar wel seyen in this world ther nas.</B><BR>
1887 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The circuit a myle was aboute,</B><BR>
1888 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Walled of stoon, and dyched al withoute.</B><BR>
1889 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Round was the shap, in manere of compas,</B><BR>
1890 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful of degrees, the heighte of sixty pas,</B><BR>
1891 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That whan a man was set on o degree,</B><BR>
1892 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He letted nat his felawe for to see.</B><BR>
1893 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Estward ther stood a gate of marbul whit,</B><BR>
1894 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Westward right swich another in the opposit.</B><BR>
1895 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And shortly to concluden, swich a place</B><BR>
1896 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Was noon in erthe, as in so litel space;</B><BR>
1897 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For in the lond ther was no crafty man</B><BR>
1898 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That geometrie or ars-metrike kan,</B><BR>
1899 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne portreyour, ne kervere of ymages,</B><BR>
1900 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That Theseus ne yaf him mete and wages</B><BR>
1901 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The theatre for to maken and devyse.</B><BR>
1902 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And for to doon his ryte and sacrifise,</B><BR>
1903 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He estward hath, upon the gate above,</B><BR>
1904 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In worshipe of Venus, goddesse of love,</B><BR>
1905 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Doon make an auter and an oratorie;</B><BR>
1906 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And on the gate westward, in memorie</B><BR>
1907 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of Mars, he maked hath right swich another,</B><BR>
1908 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That coste largely of gold a fother.</B><BR>
1909 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And northward, in a touret on the wal,</B><BR>
1910 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of alabastre whit and reed coral,</B><BR>
1911 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>An oratorie, riche for to see,</B><BR>
1912 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In worshipe of Dyane of chastitee,</B><BR>
1913 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hath Theseus doon wroght in noble wyse.</B><BR>
1914 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But yet hadde I foryeten to devyse</B><BR>
1915 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The noble kervyng and the portreitures,</B><BR>
1916 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The shap, the contenaunce, and the figures</B><BR>
1917 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That weren in thise oratories thre.</B><BR>
1918 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>First in the temple of Venus maystow se</B><BR>
1919 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wroght on the wal, ful pitous to biholde,</B><BR>
1920 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The broken slepes, and the sikes colde,</B><BR>
1921 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The sacred teeris, and the waymentynge,</B><BR>
1922 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The firy strokes of the desirynge</B><BR>
1923 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That loves servantz in this lyf enduren;</B><BR>
1924 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The othes that hir covenantz assuren;</B><BR>
1925 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Pleasance and Hope, Desir, Foolhardynesse,</B><BR>
1926 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Beautee and Youthe, Bauderie, Richesse,</B><BR>
1927 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Charmes and Force, Lesynges, Flaterye,</B><BR>
1928 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Despense, Bisynesse, and Jalousye,</B><BR>
1929 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That wered of yelewe gooldes a gerland,</B><BR>
1930 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And a cokkow sittynge on hir hand;</B><BR>
1931 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Festes, instrumentz, caroles, daunces,</B><BR>
1932 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lust and array, and alle the circumstaunces</B><BR>
1933 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of love, which that I rekned and rekne shal,</B><BR>
1934 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>By ordre weren peynted on the wal,</B><BR>
1935 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And mo than I kan make of mencioun.</B><BR>
1936 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For soothly al the mount of Citheroun,</B><BR>
1937 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther Venus hath hir principal dwellynge,</B><BR>
1938 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Was shewed on the wal in portreyynge,</B><BR>
1939 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With al the gardyn and the lustynesse.</B><BR>
1940 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Nat was foryeten the porter, Ydelnesse,</B><BR>
1941 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne Narcisus the faire of yore agon,</B><BR>
1942 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne yet the folye of kyng Salomon,</B><BR>
1943 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne yet the grete strengthe of Ercules --</B><BR>
1944 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Th'enchauntementz of Medea and Circes --</B><BR>
1945 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne of Turnus, with the hardy fiers corage,</B><BR>
1946 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The riche Cresus, kaytyf in servage.</B><BR>
1947 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thus may ye seen that wysdom ne richesse,</B><BR>
1948 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Beautee ne sleighte, strengthe ne hardynesse,</B><BR>
1949 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne may with Venus holde champartie,</B><BR>
1950 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For as hir list the world than may she gye.</B><BR>
1951 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lo, alle thise folk so caught were in hir las,</B><BR>
1952 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Til they for wo ful ofte seyde "allas!"</B><BR>
1953 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Suffiseth heere ensamples oon or two,</B><BR>
1954 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And though I koude rekene a thousand mo.</B><BR>
1955 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The statue of Venus, glorious for to se,</B><BR>
1956 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Was naked, fletynge in the large see,</B><BR>
1957 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And fro the navele doun al covered was</B><BR>
1958 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With wawes grene, and brighte as any glas.</B><BR>
1959 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A citole in hir right hand hadde she,</B><BR>
1960 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And on hir heed, ful semely for to se,</B><BR>
1961 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A rose gerland, fressh and wel smellynge;</B><BR>
1962 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Above hir heed hir dowves flikerynge.</B><BR>
1963 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Biforn hire stood hir sone Cupido;</B><BR>
1964 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon his shuldres wynges hadde he two,</B><BR>
1965 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And blynd he was, as it is often seene;</B><BR>
1966 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A bowe he bar and arwes brighte and kene.</B><BR>
1967 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Why sholde I noght as wel eek telle yow al</B><BR>
1968 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The portreiture that was upon the wal</B><BR>
1969 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Withinne the temple of myghty Mars the rede?</B><BR>
1970 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al peynted was the wal, in lengthe and brede,</B><BR>
1971 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lyk to the estres of the grisly place</B><BR>
1972 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That highte the grete temple of Mars in Trace,</B><BR>
1973 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In thilke colde, frosty regioun</B><BR>
1974 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther as Mars hath his sovereyn mansioun.</B><BR>
1975 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>First on the wal was peynted a forest,</B><BR>
1976 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In which ther dwelleth neither man ne best,</B><BR>
1977 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With knotty, knarry, bareyne trees olde,</B><BR>
1978 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of stubbes sharpe and hidouse to biholde,</B><BR>
1979 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In which ther ran a rumbel in a swough,</B><BR>
1980 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As though a storm sholde bresten every bough.</B><BR>
1981 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And dounward from an hille, under a bente,</B><BR>
1982 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther stood the temple of Mars armypotente,</B><BR>
1983 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wroght al of burned steel, of which the entree</B><BR>
1984 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Was long and streit, and gastly for to se.</B><BR>
1985 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And therout came a rage and swich a veze</B><BR>
1986 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That it made al the gate for to rese.</B><BR>
1987 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The northren lyght in at the dores shoon,</B><BR>
1988 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For wyndowe on the wal ne was ther noon,</B><BR>
1989 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thurgh which men myghten any light discerne.</B><BR>
1990 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The dore was al of adamant eterne,</B><BR>
1991 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yclenched overthwart and endelong</B><BR>
1992 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With iren tough; and for to make it strong,</B><BR>
1993 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Every pyler, the temple to sustene,</B><BR>
1994 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Was tonne-greet, of iren bright and shene.</B><BR>
1995 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther saugh I first the derke ymaginyng</B><BR>
1996 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of Felonye, and al the compassyng;</B><BR>
1997 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The crueel Ire, reed as any gleede;</B><BR>
1998 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The pykepurs, and eek the pale Drede;</B><BR>
1999 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The smylere with the knyf under the cloke;</B><BR>
2000 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The shepne brennynge with the blake smoke;</B><BR>
2001 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The tresoun of the mordrynge in the bedde;</B><BR>
2002 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The open werre, with woundes al bibledde;</B><BR>
2003 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Contek, with blody knyf and sharp manace.</B><BR>
2004 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al ful of chirkyng was that sory place.</B><BR>
2005 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The sleere of hymself yet saugh I ther --</B><BR>
2006 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His herte-blood hath bathed al his heer --</B><BR>
2007 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The nayl ydryven in the shode anyght;</B><BR>
2008 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The colde deeth, with mouth gapyng upright.</B><BR>
2009 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Amyddes of the temple sat Meschaunce,</B><BR>
2010 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With disconfort and sory contenaunce.</B><BR>
2011 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yet saugh I Woodnesse, laughynge in his rage,</B><BR>
2012 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Armed Compleint, Outhees, and fiers Outrage;</B><BR>
2013 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The careyne in the busk, with throte ycorve;</B><BR>
2014 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A thousand slayn, and nat of qualm ystorve;</B><BR>
2015 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The tiraunt, with the pray by force yraft;</B><BR>
2016 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The toun destroyed, ther was no thyng laft.</B><BR>
2017 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yet saugh I brent the shippes hoppesteres;</B><BR>
2018 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The hunte strangled with the wilde beres;</B><BR>
2019 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The sowe freten the child right in the cradel;</B><BR>
2020 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The cook yscalded, for al his longe ladel.</B><BR>
2021 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Noght was foryeten by the infortune of Marte.</B><BR>
2022 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The cartere overryden with his carte --</B><BR>
2023 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Under the wheel ful lowe he lay adoun.</B><BR>
2024 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther were also, of Martes divisioun,</B><BR>
2025 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The barbour, and the bocher, and the smyth,</B><BR>
2026 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That forgeth sharpe swerdes on his styth.</B><BR>
2027 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And al above, depeynted in a tour,</B><BR>
2028 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Saugh I Conquest, sittynge in greet honour,</B><BR>
2029 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With the sharpe swerd over his heed</B><BR>
2030 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hangynge by a soutil twynes threed.</B><BR>
2031 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Depeynted was the slaughtre of Julius,</B><BR>
2032 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of grete Nero, and of Antonius;</B><BR>
2033 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al be that thilke tyme they were unborn,</B><BR>
2034 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yet was hir deth depeynted ther-biforn</B><BR>
2035 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>By manasynge of Mars, right by figure;</B><BR>
2036 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So was it shewed in that portreiture,</B><BR>
2037 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As is depeynted in the sterres above</B><BR>
2038 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Who shal be slayn or elles deed for love.</B><BR>
2039 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Suffiseth oon ensample in stories olde;</B><BR>
2040 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I may nat rekene hem alle though I wolde.</B><BR>
2041 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The statue of Mars upon a carte stood</B><BR>
2042 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Armed, and looked grym as he were wood;</B><BR>
2043 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And over his heed ther shynen two figures</B><BR>
2044 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of sterres, that been cleped in scriptures,</B><BR>
2045 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That oon Puella, that oother Rubeus --</B><BR>
2046 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This god of armes was arrayed thus.</B><BR>
2047 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A wolf ther stood biforn hym at his feet</B><BR>
2048 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With eyen rede, and of a man he eet;</B><BR>
2049 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With soutil pencel was depeynted this storie</B><BR>
2050 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In redoutynge of Mars and of his glorie.</B><BR>
2051 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now to the temple of Dyane the chaste,</B><BR>
2052 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As shortly as I kan, I wol me haste,</B><BR>
2053 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To telle yow al the descripsioun.</B><BR>
2054 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Depeynted been the walles up and doun</B><BR>
2055 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of huntyng and of shamefast chastitee.</B><BR>
2056 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther saugh I how woful Calistopee,</B><BR>
2057 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan that Diane agreved was with here,</B><BR>
2058 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Was turned from a womman til a bere,</B><BR>
2059 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And after was she maad the loode-sterre.</B><BR>
2060 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thus was it peynted; I kan sey yow no ferre.</B><BR>
2061 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hir sone is eek a sterre, as men may see.</B><BR>
2062 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther saugh I Dane, yturned til a tree --</B><BR>
2063 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I mene nat the goddesse Diane,</B><BR>
2064 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But Penneus doghter, which that highte Dane.</B><BR>
2065 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther saugh I Attheon an hert ymaked,</B><BR>
2066 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For vengeaunce that he saugh Diane al naked;</B><BR>
2067 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I saugh how that his houndes have hym caught</B><BR>
2068 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And freeten hym, for that they knewe hym naught.</B><BR>
2069 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yet peynted was a litel forther moor</B><BR>
2070 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>How Atthalante hunted the wilde boor,</B><BR>
2071 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Meleagre, and many another mo,</B><BR>
2072 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For which Dyane wroghte hym care and wo.</B><BR>
2073 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther saugh I many another wonder storie,</B><BR>
2074 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The which me list nat drawen to memorie.</B><BR>
2075 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This goddesse on an hert ful hye seet,</B><BR>
2076 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With smale houndes al aboute hir feet,</B><BR>
2077 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And undernethe hir feet she hadde a moone --</B><BR>
2078 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wexynge it was and sholde wanye soone.</B><BR>
2079 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In gaude grene hir statue clothed was,</B><BR>
2080 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With bowe in honde and arwes in a cas.</B><BR>
2081 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hir eyen caste she ful lowe adoun</B><BR>
2082 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther Pluto hath his derke regioun.</B><BR>
2083 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A womman travaillynge was hire biforn;</B><BR>
2084 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But for hir child so longe was unborn,</B><BR>
2085 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful pitously Lucyna gan she calle</B><BR>
2086 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And seyde, "Help, for thou mayst best of alle!"</B><BR>
2087 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wel koude he peynten lifly that it wroghte;</B><BR>
2088 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With many a floryn he the hewes boghte.</B><BR>
2089 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now been thise lystes maad, and Theseus,</B><BR>
2090 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That at his grete cost arrayed thus</B><BR>
2091 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The temples and the theatre every deel,</B><BR>
2092 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan it was doon, hym lyked wonder weel.</B><BR>
2093 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But stynte I wole of Theseus a lite,</B><BR>
2094 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And speke of Palamon and of Arcite.</B><BR>
2095 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The day approcheth of hir retournynge,</B><BR>
2096 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That everich sholde an hundred knyghtes brynge</B><BR>
2097 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The bataille to darreyne, as I yow tolde.</B><BR>
2098 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And til Atthenes, hir covenant for to holde,</B><BR>
2099 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hath everich of hem broght an hundred knyghtes,</B><BR>
2100 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wel armed for the werre at alle rightes.</B><BR>
2101 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And sikerly ther trowed many a man</B><BR>
2102 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That nevere, sithen that the world bigan,</B><BR>
2103 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As for to speke of knyghthod of hir hond,</B><BR>
2104 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As fer as God hath maked see or lond,</B><BR>
2105 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Nas of so fewe so noble a compaignye.</B><BR>
2106 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For every wight that lovede chivalrye</B><BR>
2107 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And wolde, his thankes, han a passant name,</B><BR>
2108 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hath preyed that he myghte been of that game;</B><BR>
2109 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And wel was hym that therto chosen was,</B><BR>
2110 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For if ther fille tomorwe swich a cas,</B><BR>
2111 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ye knowen wel that every lusty knyght</B><BR>
2112 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That loveth paramours and hath his myght,</B><BR>
2113 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Were it in Engelond or elleswhere,</B><BR>
2114 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>They wolde, hir thankes, wilnen to be there --</B><BR>
2115 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To fighte for a lady, benedicitee!</B><BR>
2116 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>It were a lusty sighte for to see.</B><BR>
2117 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And right so ferden they with Palamon.</B><BR>
2118 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With hym ther wenten knyghtes many on;</B><BR>
2119 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Som wol ben armed in an haubergeoun,</B><BR>
2120 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in a brestplate and a light gypoun;</B><BR>
2121 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And som wol have a paire plates large;</B><BR>
2122 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And som wol have a Pruce sheeld or a targe;</B><BR>
2123 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Som wol ben armed on his legges weel,</B><BR>
2124 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And have an ax, and som a mace of steel --</B><BR>
2125 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther is no newe gyse that it nas old.</B><BR>
2126 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Armed were they, as I have yow told,</B><BR>
2127 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Everych after his opinioun.</B><BR>
2128 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther maistow seen, comynge with Palamoun,</B><BR>
2129 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lygurge hymself, the grete kyng of Trace.</B><BR>
2130 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Blak was his berd, and manly was his face;</B><BR>
2131 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The cercles of his eyen in his heed,</B><BR>
2132 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>They gloweden bitwixen yelow and reed,</B><BR>
2133 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And lik a grifphon looked he aboute,</B><BR>
2134 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With kempe heeris on his browes stoute;</B><BR>
2135 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His lymes grete, his brawnes harde and stronge,</B><BR>
2136 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His shuldres brode, his armes rounde and longe;</B><BR>
2137 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And as the gyse was in his contree,</B><BR>
2138 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful hye upon a chaar of gold stood he,</B><BR>
2139 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With foure white boles in the trays.</B><BR>
2140 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In stede of cote-armure over his harnays,</B><BR>
2141 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With nayles yelewe and brighte as any gold,</B><BR>
2142 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He hadde a beres skyn, col-blak for old.</B><BR>
2143 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His longe heer was kembd bihynde his bak;</B><BR>
2144 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As any ravenes fethere it shoon for blak;</B><BR>
2145 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A wrethe of gold, arm-greet, of huge wighte,</B><BR>
2146 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon his heed, set ful of stones brighte,</B><BR>
2147 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of fyne rubyes and of dyamauntz.</B><BR>
2148 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Aboute his chaar ther wenten white alauntz,</B><BR>
2149 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Twenty and mo, as grete as any steer,</B><BR>
2150 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To hunten at the leoun or the deer,</B><BR>
2151 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And folwed hym with mosel faste ybounde,</B><BR>
2152 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Colered of gold, and tourettes fyled rounde.</B><BR>
2153 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>An hundred lordes hadde he in his route,</B><BR>
2154 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Armed ful wel, with hertes stierne and stoute.</B><BR>
2155 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With Arcita, in stories as men fynde,</B><BR>
2156 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The grete Emetreus, the kyng of Inde,</B><BR>
2157 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon a steede bay trapped in steel,</B><BR>
2158 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Covered in clooth of gold, dyapred weel,</B><BR>
2159 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Cam ridynge lyk the god of armes, Mars.</B><BR>
2160 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His cote-armure was of clooth of Tars</B><BR>
2161 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Couched with perles white and rounde and grete;</B><BR>
2162 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His sadel was of brend gold newe ybete;</B><BR>
2163 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A mantelet upon his shulder hangynge,</B><BR>
2164 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bret-ful of rubyes rede as fyr sparklynge;</B><BR>
2165 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His crispe heer lyk rynges was yronne,</B><BR>
2166 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And that was yelow, and glytered as the sonne.</B><BR>
2167 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His nose was heigh, his eyen bright citryn,</B><BR>
2168 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His lippes rounde, his colour was sangwyn;</B><BR>
2169 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A fewe frakenes in his face yspreynd,</B><BR>
2170 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bitwixen yelow and somdel blak ymeynd;</B><BR>
2171 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And as a leon he his lookyng caste.</B><BR>
2172 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of fyve and twenty yeer his age I caste.</B><BR>
2173 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His berd was wel bigonne for to sprynge;</B><BR>
2174 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His voys was as a trompe thonderynge.</B><BR>
2175 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon his heed he wered of laurer grene</B><BR>
2176 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A gerland, fressh and lusty for to sene.	</B><BR>
2177 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon his hand he bar for his deduyt</B><BR>
2178 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>An egle tame, as any lilye whyt.</B><BR>
2179 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>An hundred lordes hadde he with hym there,</B><BR>
2180 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al armed, save hir heddes, in al hir gere,</B><BR>
2181 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful richely in alle maner thynges.</B><BR>
2182 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For trusteth wel that dukes, erles, kynges</B><BR>
2183 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Were gadered in this noble compaignye,</B><BR>
2184 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For love and for encrees of chivalrye.</B><BR>
2185 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Aboute this kyng ther ran on every part</B><BR>
2186 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful many a tame leon and leopart.</B><BR>
2187 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in this wise thise lordes, alle and some,</B><BR>
2188 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Been on the Sonday to the citee come</B><BR>
2189 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Aboute pryme, and in the toun alight.</B><BR>
2190 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This Theseus, this duc, this worthy knyght,</B><BR>
2191 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan he had broght hem into his citee,</B><BR>
2192 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And inned hem, everich at his degree,</B><BR>
2193 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He festeth hem, and dooth so greet labour</B><BR>
2194 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To esen hem and doon hem al honour</B><BR>
2195 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That yet men wenen that no mannes wit</B><BR>
2196 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of noon estaat ne koude amenden it.</B><BR>
2197 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The mynstralcye, the service at the feeste,</B><BR>
2198 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The grete yiftes to the meeste and leeste,</B><BR>
2199 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The riche array of Theseus paleys,</B><BR>
2200 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne who sat first ne last upon the deys,</B><BR>
2201 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>What ladyes fairest been or best daunsynge,</B><BR>
2202 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Or which of hem kan dauncen best and synge,</B><BR>
2203 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne who moost felyngly speketh of love;</B><BR>
2204 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>What haukes sitten on the perche above,</B><BR>
2205 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>What houndes liggen on the floor adoun --</B><BR>
2206 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of al this make I now no mencioun,</B><BR>
2207 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>But al th' effect; that thynketh me the beste.</B><BR>
2208 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now cometh the point, and herkneth if yow leste.</B><BR>
2209 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The Sonday nyght, er day bigan to sprynge,</B><BR>
2210 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan Palamon the larke herde synge</B><BR>
2211 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>(Although it nere nat day by houres two,</B><BR>
2212 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yet the larke sang) and Palamon right then</B><BR>
2213 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With hooly herte and with an heigh corage,</B><BR>
2214 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He roos to wenden on his pilgrymage</B><BR>
2215 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Unto the blissful Citherea benign --</B><BR>
2216 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I mene Venus, honurable and digne.</B><BR>
2217 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in hir houre he walketh forth a pas</B><BR>
2218 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Unto the lystes ther hire temple was,</B><BR>
2219 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And doun he kneleth, and with humble cheere</B><BR>
2220 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And herte soor he seyde as ye shal heere:</B><BR>
2221 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Faireste of faire, O lady myn, Venus,</B><BR>
2222 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Doughter to Jove and spouse of Vulcanus,</B><BR>
2223 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thow gladere of the mount of Citheron,</B><BR>
2224 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For thilke love thow haddest to Adoon,</B><BR>
2225 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Have pitee of my bittre teeris smerte,</B><BR>
2226 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And taak myn humble preyere at thyn herte.</B><BR>
2227 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Allas! I ne have no langage to telle</B><BR>
2228 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Th'effectes ne the tormentz of myn helle;</B><BR>
2229 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Myn herte may myne harmes nat biwreye;</B><BR>
2230 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I am so confus that I kan noght seye</B><BR>
2231 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But `Mercy, lady bright, that knowest weele</B><BR>
2232 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>My thought and seest what harmes that I feele!'</B><BR>
2233 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Considere al this and rewe upon my soore,</B><BR>
2234 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As wisly as I shal for everemoore,</B><BR>
2235 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Emforth my myght, thy trewe servant be,</B><BR>
2236 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And holden werre alwey with chastitee.</B><BR>
2237 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That make I myn avow, so ye me helpe!</B><BR>
2238 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I kepe noght of armes for to yelpe,</B><BR>
2239 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne I ne axe nat tomorwe to have victorie,</B><BR>
2240 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne renoun in this cas, ne veyne glorie</B><BR>
2241 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of pris of armes blowen up and doun;</B><BR>
2242 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But I wolde have fully possessioun</B><BR>
2243 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of Emelye, and dye in thy servyse.</B><BR>
2244 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Fynd thow the manere hou and in what wyse:</B><BR>
2245 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I recche nat but it may bettre be</B><BR>
2246 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To have victorie of hem, or they of me,</B><BR>
2247 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So that I have my lady in myne armes.</B><BR>
2248 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For though so be that Mars is god of armes,</B><BR>
2249 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Youre vertu is so greet in hevene above</B><BR>
2250 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That if yow list, I shal wel have my love.</B><BR>
2251 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thy temple wol I worshipe everemo,</B><BR>
2252 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And on thyn auter, where I ride or go,</B><BR>
2253 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I wol doon sacrifice and fires beete.</B><BR>
2254 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And if ye wol nat so, my lady sweete,</B><BR>
2255 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne preye I thee, tomorwe with a spere</B><BR>
2256 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That Arcita me thurgh the herte bere.</B><BR>
2257 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne rekke I noght, whan I have lost my lyf,</B><BR>
2258 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Though that Arcita wynne hire to his wyf.</B><BR>
2259 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This is th'effect and ende of my preyere:</B><BR>
2260 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yif me my love, thow blisful lady deere."</B><BR>
2261 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan the orison was doon of Palamon,</B><BR>
2262 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His sacrifice he dide, and that anon,</B><BR>
2263 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful pitously, with alle circumstaunces,</B><BR>
2264 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al telle I noght as now his observaunces;</B><BR>
2265 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But atte laste the statue of Venus shook,</B><BR>
2266 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And made a signe, wherby that he took</B><BR>
2267 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That his preyere accepted was that day.</B><BR>
2268 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For thogh the signe shewed a delay,</B><BR>
2269 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yet wiste he wel that graunted was his boone,</B><BR>
2270 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with glad herte he wente hym hoom ful soone.</B><BR>
2271 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The thridde houre inequal that Palamon</B><BR>
2272 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bigan to Venus temple for to gon,</B><BR>
2273 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Up roos the sonne, and up roos Emelye</B><BR>
2274 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And to the temple of Dyane gan hye.</B><BR>
2275 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hir maydens, that she thider with hire ladde,</B><BR>
2276 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful redily with hem the fyr they hadde,</B><BR>
2277 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Th'encens, the clothes, and the remenant al</B><BR>
2278 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That to the sacrifice longen shal;</B><BR>
2279 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The hornes fulle of meeth, as was the gyse --</B><BR>
2280 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther lakked noght to doon hir sacrifise.</B><BR>
2281 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Smokynge the temple, ful of clothes faire,</B><BR>
2282 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This Emelye, with herte debonaire,</B><BR>
2283 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hir body wessh with water of a welle.</B><BR>
2284 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But hou she dide hir ryte I dar nat telle,</B><BR>
2285 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But it be any thing in general;</B><BR>
2286 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And yet it were a game to heeren al.</B><BR>
2287 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To hym that meneth wel it were no charge;</B><BR>
2288 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But it is good a man been at his large.</B><BR>
2289 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hir brighte heer was kembd, untressed al;</B><BR>
2290 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A coroune of a grene ook cerial</B><BR>
2291 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon hir heed was set ful fair and meete.</B><BR>
2292 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Two fyres on the auter gan she beete,</B><BR>
2293 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And dide hir thynges, as men may biholde</B><BR>
2294 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;     <B>In Stace of Thebes and thise bookes olde.</B><BR>
2295 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan kyndled was the fyr, with pitous cheere</B><BR>
2296 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Unto Dyane she spak as ye may heere:</B><BR>
2297 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"O chaste goddesse of the wodes grene,</B><BR>
2298 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To whom bothe hevene and erthe and see is sene,</B><BR>
2299 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Queene of the regne of Pluto derk and lowe,</B><BR>
2300 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Goddesse of maydens, that myn herte hast knowe</B><BR>
2301 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful many a yeer, and woost what I desire,</B><BR>
2302 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As keepe me fro thy vengeaunce and thyn ire,</B><BR>
2303 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That Attheon aboughte cruelly.</B><BR>
2304 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Chaste goddesse, wel wostow that I</B><BR>
2305 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Desire to ben a mayden al my lyf,</B><BR>
2306 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne nevere wol I be no love ne wyf.</B><BR>
2307 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I am, thow woost, yet of thy compaignye,</B><BR>
2308 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A mayde, and love huntynge and venerye,</B><BR>
2309 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And for to walken in the wodes wilde,</B><BR>
2310 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And noght to ben a wyf and be with childe.</B><BR>
2311 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Noght wol I knowe compaignye of man.</B><BR>
2312 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now help me, lady, sith ye may and kan,</B><BR>
2313 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For tho thre formes that thou hast in thee.</B><BR>
2314 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Palamon, that hath swich love to me,</B><BR>
2315 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek Arcite, that loveth me so soore,</B><BR>
2316 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This grace I preye thee withoute moore,</B><BR>
2317 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As sende love and pees bitwixe hem two,</B><BR>
2318 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And fro me turne awey hir hertes so</B><BR>
2319 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That al hire hoote love and hir desir,</B><BR>
2320 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And al hir bisy torment, and hir fir</B><BR>
2321 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Be queynt, or turned in another place.</B><BR>
2322 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And if so be thou wolt nat do me grace,</B><BR>
2323 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Or if my destynee be shapen so</B><BR>
2324 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That I shal nedes have oon of hem two,</B><BR>
2325 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As sende me hym that moost desireth me.</B><BR>
2326 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bihoold, goddesse of clene chastitee,</B><BR>
2327 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The bittre teeris that on my chekes falle.</B><BR>
2328 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Syn thou art mayde and kepere of us alle,</B><BR>
2329 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>My maydenhede thou kepe and wel conserve,</B><BR>
2330 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And whil I lyve, a mayde I wol thee serve."</B><BR>
2331 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The fires brenne upon the auter cleere,</B><BR>
2332 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whil Emelye was thus in hir preyere.</B><BR>
2333 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But sodeynly she saugh a sighte queynte,</B><BR>
2334 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For right anon oon of the fyres queynte</B><BR>
2335 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And quyked agayn, and after that anon</B><BR>
2336 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That oother fyr was queynt and al agon;</B><BR>
2337 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And as it queynte it made a whistelynge,</B><BR>
2338 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As doon thise wete brondes in hir brennynge,</B><BR>
2339 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And at the brondes ende out ran anon</B><BR>
2340 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As it were blody dropes many oon;</B><BR>
2341 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For which so soore agast was Emelye</B><BR>
2342 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That she was wel ny mad and gan to crye,</B><BR>
2343 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For she ne wiste what it signyfied,</B><BR>
2344 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But oonly for the feere thus hath she cried,</B><BR>
2345 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And weep that it was pitee for to heere.</B><BR>
2346 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And therwithal Dyane gan appeere,</B><BR>
2347 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With bowe in honde, right as an hunteresse,</B><BR>
2348 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And seyde, "Doghter, stynt thyn hevynesse.</B><BR>
2349 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Among the goddes hye it is affermed,</B><BR>
2350 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And by eterne word writen and confermed,</B><BR>
2351 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thou shalt ben wedded unto oon of tho</B><BR>
2352 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That han for thee so muchel care and wo,</B><BR>
2353 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But unto which of hem I may nat telle.</B><BR>
2354 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Farwel, for I ne may no lenger dwelle.</B><BR>
2355 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The fires which that on myn auter brenne</B><BR>
2356 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Shulle thee declaren, er that thou go henne,</B><BR>
2357 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thyn aventure of love, as in this cas."</B><BR>
2358 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with that word, the arwes in the caas</B><BR>
2359 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of the goddesse clateren faste and rynge,</B><BR>
2360 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And forth she wente and made a vanysshynge;</B><BR>
2361 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For which this Emelye astoned was,</B><BR>
2362 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And seyde, "What amounteth this, allas?</B><BR>
2363 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I putte me in thy proteccioun,</B><BR>
2364 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Dyane, and in thy disposicioun."</B><BR>
2365 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And hoom she goth anon the nexte weye.</B><BR>
2366 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This is th'effect; ther is namoore to seye.</B><BR>
2367 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The nexte houre of Mars folwynge this,</B><BR>
2368 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Arcite unto the temple walked is</B><BR>
2369 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of fierse Mars to doon his sacrifise,</B><BR>
2370 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With alle the rytes of his payen wyse.</B><BR>
2371 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With pitous herte and heigh devocioun,</B><BR>
2372 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Right thus to Mars he seyde his orisoun:</B><BR>
2373 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"O stronge god, that in the regnes colde</B><BR>
2374 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of Trace honoured art and lord yholde,</B><BR>
2375 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And hast in every regne and every lond</B><BR>
2376 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of armes al the brydel in thyn hond,</B><BR>
2377 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And hem fortunest as thee lyst devyse,</B><BR>
2378 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Accepte of me my pitous sacrifise.</B><BR>
2379 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>If so be that my youthe may deserve,</B><BR>
2380 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And that my myght be worthy for to serve</B><BR>
2381 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thy godhede, that I may been oon of thyne,</B><BR>
2382 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne preye I thee to rewe upon my pyne.</B><BR>
2383 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For thilke peyne and thilke hoote fir</B><BR>
2384 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In which thow whilom brendest for desir,</B><BR>
2385 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan that thow usedest the beautee</B><BR>
2386 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of faire, yonge, fresshe Venus free,</B><BR>
2387 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And haddest hire in armes at thy wille --</B><BR>
2388 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Although thee ones on a tyme mysfille,</B><BR>
2389 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan Vulcanus hadde caught thee in his las</B><BR>
2390 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And foond thee liggynge by his wyf, allas! --</B><BR>
2391 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For thilke sorwe that was in thyn herte,</B><BR>
2392 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Have routhe as wel upon my peynes smerte.</B><BR>
2393 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I am yong and unkonnynge, as thow woost,</B><BR>
2394 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And, as I trowe, with love offended moost</B><BR>
2395 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That evere was any lyves creature,</B><BR>
2396 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For she that dooth me al this wo endure</B><BR>
2397 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne reccheth nevere wher I synke or fleete.</B><BR>
2398 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And wel I woot, er she me mercy heete,</B><BR>
2399 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I moot with strengthe wynne hire in the place,</B><BR>
2400 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And wel I woot, withouten help or grace</B><BR>
2401 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of thee ne may my strengthe noght availle.</B><BR>
2402 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanne help me, lord, tomorwe in my bataille,</B><BR>
2403 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For thilke fyr that whilom brente thee,</B><BR>
2404 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As wel as thilke fyr now brenneth me,</B><BR>
2405 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And do that I tomorwe have victorie.</B><BR>
2406 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Myn be the travaille, and thyn be the glorie!</B><BR>
2407 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thy sovereyn temple wol I moost honouren</B><BR>
2408 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of any place, and alwey moost labouren</B><BR>
2409 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In thy plesaunce and in thy craftes stronge,</B><BR>
2410 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in thy temple I wol my baner honge</B><BR>
2411 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And alle the armes of my compaignye,</B><BR>
2412 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And everemo, unto that day I dye,</B><BR>
2413 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Eterne fir I wol bifore thee fynde.</B><BR>
2414 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek to this avow I wol me bynde:</B><BR>
2415 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>My beerd, myn heer, that hongeth long adoun,</B><BR>
2416 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That nevere yet ne felte offensioun</B><BR>
2417 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of rasour nor of shere, I wol thee yive,</B><BR>
2418 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And ben thy trewe servant whil I lyve.</B><BR>
2419 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now, lord, have routhe upon my sorwes soore;</B><BR>
2420 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yif me [victorie]; I aske thee namoore."</B><BR>
2421 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The preyere stynt of Arcita the stronge,</B><BR>
2422 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The rynges on the temple dore that honge,</B><BR>
2423 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek the dores, clatereden ful faste,</B><BR>
2424 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of which Arcita somwhat hym agaste.</B><BR>
2425 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The fyres brenden upon the auter brighte</B><BR>
2426 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That it gan al the temple for to lighte;</B><BR>
2427 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A sweete smel the ground anon up yaf,</B><BR>
2428 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Arcita anon his hand up haf,</B><BR>
2429 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And moore encens into the fyr he caste,</B><BR>
2430 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With othere rytes mo; and atte laste</B><BR>
2431 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The statue of Mars bigan his hauberk rynge,</B><BR>
2432 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with that soun he herde a murmurynge</B><BR>
2433 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful lowe and dym, and seyde thus, "Victorie!"</B><BR>
2434 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For which he yaf to Mars honour and glorie.</B><BR>
2435 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thus with joye and hope wel to fare</B><BR>
2436 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Arcite anon unto his in is fare,</B><BR>
2437 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As fayn as fowel is of the brighte sonne.</B><BR>
2438 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And right anon swich strif ther is bigonne,</B><BR>
2439 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For thilke grauntyng, in the hevene above,</B><BR>
2440 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bitwixe Venus, the goddesse of love,</B><BR>
2441 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Mars, the stierne god armypotente,</B><BR>
2442 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That Juppiter was bisy it to stente,</B><BR>
2443 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Til that the pale Saturnus the colde,</B><BR>
2444 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That knew so manye of aventures olde,</B><BR>
2445 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Foond in his olde experience an art</B><BR>
2446 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That he ful soone hath plesed every part.</B><BR>
2447 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As sooth is seyd, elde hath greet avantage;</B><BR>
2448 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In elde is bothe wysdom and usage;</B><BR>
2449 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Men may the olde atrenne and noght atrede.</B><BR>
2450 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Saturne anon, to stynten strif and drede,</B><BR>
2451 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al be it that it is agayn his kynde,</B><BR>
2452 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of al this strif he gan remedie fynde.</B><BR>
2453 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"My deere doghter Venus," quod Saturne,</B><BR>
2454 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"My cours, that hath so wyde for to turne,</B><BR>
2455 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hath moore power than woot any man.</B><BR>
2456 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Myn is the drenchyng in the see so wan;</B><BR>
2457 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Myn is the prison in the derke cote;</B><BR>
2458 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Myn is the stranglyng and hangyng by the throte,</B><BR>
2459 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The murmure and the cherles rebellyng,</B><BR>
2460 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The groynynge, and the pryvee empoysonyng;</B><BR>
2461 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I do vengeance and pleyn correccioun,</B><BR>
2462 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whil I dwelle in the signe of the leoun.</B><BR>
2463 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Myn is the ruyne of the hye halles,</B><BR>
2464 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The fallynge of the toures and of the walles</B><BR>
2465 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon the mynour or the carpenter.</B><BR>
2466 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I slow Sampsoun, shakynge the piler;</B><BR>
2467 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And myne be the maladyes colde,</B><BR>
2468 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The derke tresons, and the castes olde;</B><BR>
2469 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>My lookyng is the fader of pestilence.</B><BR>
2470 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now weep namoore; I shal doon diligence</B><BR>
2471 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That Palamon, that is thyn owene knyght,</B><BR>
2472 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Shal have his lady, as thou hast him hight.</B><BR>
2473 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Though Mars shal helpe his knyght, yet nathelees</B><BR>
2474 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bitwixe yow ther moot be som tyme pees,</B><BR>
2475 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Al be ye noght of o compleccioun,</B><BR>
2476 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That causeth al day swich divisioun.</B><BR>
2477 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I am thyn aiel, redy at thy wille;</B><BR>
2478 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Weep now namoore; I wol thy lust fulfille."</B><BR>
2479 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now wol I stynten of the goddes above,</B><BR>
2480 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of Mars, and of Venus, goddesse of love,</B><BR>
2481 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And telle yow as pleynly as I kan</B><BR>
2482 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The grete effect, for which that I bygan.</B><BR>
859 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whilom, as olde stories tellen us,</B><BR>
860 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther was a duc that highte Theseus;</B><BR>
861 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of Atthenes he was lord and governour,</B><BR>
862 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in his tyme swich a conquerour</B><BR>
863 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That gretter was ther noon under the sonne.</B><BR>
864 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ful many a riche contree hadde he wonne;</B><BR>
865 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>What with his wysdom and his chivalrie,</B><BR>
866 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He conquered al the regne of Femenye,</B><BR>
867 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That whilom was ycleped Scithia,</B><BR>
868 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And weddede the queene Ypolita,</B><BR>
869 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And broghte hire hoom with hym in his contree</B><BR>
870 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With muchel glorie and greet solempnytee,</B><BR>
871 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek hir yonge suster Emelye.</B><BR>
872 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And thus with victorie and with melodye</B><BR>
873 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lete I this noble duc to Atthenes ryde,</B><BR>
874 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And al his hoost in armes hym bisyde.</B><BR>
875 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And certes, if it nere to long to heere,</B><BR>
876 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I wolde have toold yow fully the manere</B><BR>
877 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>How wonnen was the regne of Femenye</B><BR>
878 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>By Theseus and by his chivalrye;</B><BR>
879 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And of the grete bataille for the nones</B><BR>
880 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bitwixen Atthenes and Amazones;</B><BR>
881 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And how asseged was Ypolita,</B><BR>
882 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The faire, hardy queene of Scithia;</B><BR>
883 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And of the feste that was at hir weddynge,</B><BR>
884 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And of the tempest at hir hoom-comynge;</B><BR>
885 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But al that thyng I moot as now forbere.</B><BR>
886 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I have, God woot, a large feeld to ere,</B><BR>
887 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And wayke been the oxen in my plough.</B><BR>
888 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The remenant of the tale is long ynough.</B><BR>
889 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I wol nat letten eek noon of this route;</B><BR>
890 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Lat every felawe telle his tale aboute,</B><BR>
891 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And lat se now who shal the soper wynne;</B><BR>
892 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And ther I lefte, I wol ayeyn bigynne.</B><BR>
893 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This duc, of whom I make mencioun,</B><BR>
894 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan he was come almoost unto the toun,</B><BR>
895 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In al his wele and in his mooste pride,</B><BR>
896 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He was war, as he caste his eye aside,</B><BR>
897 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Where that ther kneled in the heighe weye</B><BR>
898 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>A compaignye of ladyes, tweye and tweye,</B><BR>
899 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ech after oother clad in clothes blake;</B><BR>
900 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But swich a cry and swich a wo they make</B><BR>
901 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That in this world nys creature lyvynge</B><BR>
902 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That herde swich another waymentynge;</B><BR>
903 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And of this cry they nolde nevere stenten</B><BR>
904 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Til they the reynes of his brydel henten.</B><BR>
905 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"What folk been ye, that at myn hom-comynge</B><BR>
906 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Perturben so my feste with criynge?"</B><BR>
907 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Quod Theseus. "Have ye so greet envye</B><BR>
908 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of myn honour, that thus compleyne and crye?</B><BR>
909 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Or who hath yow mysboden or offended?</B><BR>
910 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And telleth me if it may been amended,</B><BR>
911 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And why that ye been clothed thus in blak."</B><BR>
912 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The eldeste lady of them alle spak,</B><BR>
913 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan she hadde swowned with a deedly cheere,</B><BR>
914 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That it was routhe for to seen and heere;</B><BR>
915 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>She seyde, "Lord, to whom Fortune hath yiven</B><BR>
916 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Victorie, and as a conqueror to lyven,</B><BR>
917 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Nat greveth us youre glorie and youre honour,</B><BR>
918 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But we biseken mercy and socour.</B><BR>
919 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Have mercy on oure wo and oure distresse!</B><BR>
920 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Som drope of pitee, thurgh thy gentillesse,</B><BR>
921 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon us wrecched wommen lat thou falle,</B><BR>
922 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For, certes, lord, ther is noon of us alle</B><BR>
923 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That she ne hath been a duchesse or a queene.</B><BR>
924 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now be we caytyves, as it is wel seene,</B><BR>
925 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thanked be Fortune and hire false wheel,</B><BR>
926 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That noon estaat assureth to be weel.</B><BR>
927 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And certes, lord, to abyden youre presence,</B><BR>
928 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Heere in this temple of the goddesse Clemence</B><BR>
929 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>We han ben waitynge al this fourtenyght.</B><BR>
930 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Now help us, lord, sith it is in thy myght.</B><BR>
931 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"I, wrecche, which that wepe and wayle thus,</B><BR>
932 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Was whilom wyf to kyng Cappaneus,</B><BR>
933 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That starf at Thebes -- cursed be that day! --</B><BR>
934 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And alle we that been in this array</B><BR>
935 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And maken al this lamentacioun,</B><BR>
936 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>We losten alle oure housbondes at that toun,</B><BR>
937 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whil that the seege theraboute lay.</B><BR>
938 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And yet now the olde Creon -- weylaway! --</B><BR>
939 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That lord is now of Thebes the citee,</B><BR>
940 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Fulfild of ire and of iniquitee,</B><BR>
941 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He, for despit and for his tirannye,</B><BR>
942 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To do the dede bodyes vileynye</B><BR>
943 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of alle oure lordes whiche that been yslawe,</B><BR>
944 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hath alle the bodyes on an heep ydrawe,</B><BR>
945 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And wol nat suffren hem, by noon assent,</B><BR>
946 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Neither to been yburyed nor ybrent,</B><BR>
947 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But maketh houndes ete them in despit."</B><BR>
948 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with that word, withouten moore respit,</B><BR>
949 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>They fillen gruf and criden pitously,</B><BR>
950 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Have on us wrecched wommen som mercy,</B><BR>
951 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And lat oure sorwe synken in thyn herte."</B><BR>
952 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This gentil duc doun from his courser sterte</B><BR>
953 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With herte pitous, whan he herde them speke.</B><BR>
954 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hym thoughte that his herte wolde breke,</B><BR>
955 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan he saugh hem so pitous and so maat,</B><BR>
956 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That whilom weren of so greet estaat;</B><BR>
957 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in his armes he hem alle up hente,</B><BR>
958 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And hem conforteth in ful good entente,</B><BR>
959 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And swoor his ooth, as he was trewe knyght,</B><BR>
960 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He wolde doon so ferforthly his myght</B><BR>
961 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Upon the tiraunt Creon hem to wreke</B><BR>
962 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That al the peple of Grece sholde speke</B><BR>
963 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>How Creon was of Theseus yserved</B><BR>
964 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As he that hadde his deeth ful wel deserved.</B><BR>
965 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And right anoon, withouten moore abood,</B><BR>
966 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>His baner he desplayeth, and forth rood</B><BR>
967 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To Thebes-ward, and al his hoost biside.</B><BR>
968 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>No neer Atthenes wolde he go ne ride,</B><BR>
969 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ne take his ese fully half a day,</B><BR>
970 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But onward on his wey that nyght he lay,</B><BR>
971 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And sente anon Ypolita the queene,</B><BR>
972 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Emelye, hir yonge suster sheene,</B><BR>
973 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Unto the toun of Atthenes to dwelle,</B><BR>
974 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And forth he rit; ther is namoore to telle.</B><BR>
975 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The rede statue of Mars, with spere and targe,</B><BR>
976 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So shyneth in his white baner large</B><BR>
977 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That alle the feeldes glyteren up and doun;</B><BR>
978 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And by his baner born is his penoun</B><BR>
979 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of gold ful riche, in which ther was ybete</B><BR>
980 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The Mynotaur, which that he wan in Crete.</B><BR>
981 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thus rit this duc, thus rit this conquerour,</B><BR>
982 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in his hoost of chivalrie the flour,</B><BR>
983 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Til that he cam to Thebes and alighte</B><BR>
984 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Faire in a feeld, ther as he thoughte to fighte.</B><BR>
985 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But shortly for to speken of this thyng,</B><BR>
986 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With Creon, which that was of Thebes kyng,</B><BR>
987 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He faught, and slough hym manly as a knyght</B><BR>
988 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In pleyn bataille, and putte the folk to flyght;</B><BR>
989 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And by assaut he wan the citee after,</B><BR>
990 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And rente adoun bothe wall and sparre and rafter;</B><BR>
991 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And to the ladyes he restored agayn</B><BR>
992 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The bones of hir freendes that were slayn,</B><BR>
993 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To doon obsequies, as was tho the gyse.</B><BR>
994 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But it were al to longe for to devyse</B><BR>
995 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The grete clamour and the waymentynge</B><BR>
996 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That the ladyes made at the brennynge</B><BR>
997 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of the bodies, and the grete honour</B><BR>
998 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That Theseus, the noble conquerour,</B><BR>
999 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Dooth to the ladyes, whan they from hym wente;</B><BR>
1000 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But shortly for to telle is myn entente.</B><BR>
1001 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Whan that this worthy duc, this Theseus,</B><BR>
1002 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hath Creon slayn and wonne Thebes thus,</B><BR>
1003 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; <B>Stille in that feeld he took al nyght his reste,</B><BR>
1004 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And dide with al the contree as hym leste.</B><BR>
1005 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To ransake in the taas of bodyes dede,</B><BR>
1006 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hem for to strepe of harneys and of wede,</B><BR>
1007 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The pilours diden bisynesse and cure</B><BR>
1008 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>After the bataille and disconfiture.</B><BR>
1009 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And so bifel that in the taas they founde,</B><BR>
1010 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thurgh-girt with many a grevous blody wounde,</B><BR>
1011 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Two yonge knyghtes liggynge by and by,</B><BR>
1012 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bothe in oon armes, wroght ful richely,</B><BR>
1013 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of whiche two Arcita highte that oon,</B><BR>
1014 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And that oother knyght highte Palamon.</B><BR>
1015 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Nat fully quyke, ne fully dede they were,</B><BR>
1016 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But by hir cote-armures and by hir gere</B><BR>
1017 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The heraudes knewe hem best in special</B><BR>
1018 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As they that weren of the blood roial</B><BR>
1019 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of Thebes, and of sustren two yborn.</B><BR>
1020 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Out of the taas the pilours han hem torn,</B><BR>
1021 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And han hem caried softe unto the tente</B><BR>
1022 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of Theseus; and he ful soone hem sente</B><BR>
1023 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To Atthenes, to dwellen in prisoun</B><BR>
1024 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Perpetuelly -- he nolde no raunsoun.</B><BR>
1025 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And whan this worthy duc hath thus ydon,</B><BR>
1026 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He took his hoost, and hoom he rit anon</B><BR>
1027 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>With laurer crowned as a conquerour;</B><BR>
1028 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And ther he lyveth in joye and in honour</B><BR>
1029 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Terme of his lyf; what nedeth wordes mo?</B><BR>
1030 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in a tour, in angwissh and in wo,</B><BR>
1031 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This Palamon and his felawe Arcite</B><BR>
1032 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For everemoore; ther may no gold hem quite.</B><BR>
1033 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This passeth yeer by yeer and day by day,</B><BR>
1034 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Till it fil ones, in a morwe of May,</B><BR>
1035 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That Emelye, that fairer was to sene</B><BR>
1036 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Than is the lylie upon his stalke grene,</B><BR>
1037 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And fressher than the May with floures newe --</B><BR>
1038 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For with the rose colour stroof hire hewe,</B><BR>
1039 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I noot which was the fyner of hem two --</B><BR>
1040 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Er it were day, as was hir wone to do,</B><BR>
1041 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>She was arisen and al redy dight,</B><BR>
1042 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For May wole have no slogardie anyght.</B><BR>
1043 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The sesoun priketh every gentil herte,</B><BR>
1044 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And maketh it out of his slep to sterte,</B><BR>
1045 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And seith "Arys, and do thyn observaunce."</B><BR>
1046 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This maked Emelye have remembraunce</B><BR>
1047 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To doon honour to May, and for to ryse.</B><BR>
1048 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yclothed was she fressh, for to devyse:</B><BR>
1049 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hir yelow heer was broyded in a tresse</B><BR>
1050 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bihynde hir bak, a yerde long, I gesse.</B><BR>
1051 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And in the gardyn, at the sonne upriste,</B><BR>
1052 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>She walketh up and doun, and as hire liste</B><BR>
1053 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>She gadereth floures, party white and rede,</B><BR>
1054 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>To make a subtil gerland for hire hede;</B><BR>
1055 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And as an aungel hevenysshly she soong.</B><BR>
1056 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The grete tour, that was so thikke and stroong,</B><BR>
1057 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Which of the castel was the chief dongeoun</B><BR>
1058 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>(Ther as the knyghtes weren in prisoun</B><BR>
1059 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of which I tolde yow and tellen shal),</B><BR>
1060 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Was evene joynant to the gardyn wal</B><BR>
1061 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther as this Emelye hadde hir pleyynge.</B><BR>
1062 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bright was the sonne and cleer that morwenynge,</B><BR>
1063 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And Palamoun, this woful prisoner,</B><BR>
1064 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As was his wone, by leve of his gayler,</B><BR>
1065 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Was risen and romed in a chambre an heigh,</B><BR>
1066 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>In which he al the noble citee seigh,</B><BR>
1067 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And eek the gardyn, ful of braunches grene,</B><BR>
1068 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Ther as this fresshe Emelye the shene</B><BR>
1069 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Was in hire walk, and romed up and doun.</B><BR>
1070 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This sorweful prisoner, this Palamoun,</B><BR>
1071 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Goth in the chambre romynge to and fro</B><BR>
1072 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And to hymself compleynynge of his wo.</B><BR>
1073 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That he was born, ful ofte he seyde, "allas!"</B><BR>
1074 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And so bifel, by aventure or cas,</B><BR>
1075 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That thurgh a wyndow, thikke of many a barre</B><BR>
1076 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of iren greet and square as any sparre,</B><BR>
1077 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>He cast his eye upon Emelya,</B><BR>
1078 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And therwithal he bleynte and cride, "A!"</B><BR>
1079 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>As though he stongen were unto the herte.</B><BR>
1080 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with that cry Arcite anon up sterte</B><BR>
1081 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And seyde, "Cosyn myn, what eyleth thee,</B><BR>
1082 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That art so pale and deedly on to see?</B><BR>
1083 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Why cridestow? Who hath thee doon offence?</B><BR>
1084 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>For Goddes love, taak al in pacience</B><BR>
1085 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Oure prisoun, for it may noon oother be.</B><BR>
1086 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Fortune hath yeven us this adversitee.</B><BR>
1087 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Som wikke aspect or disposicioun</B><BR>
1088 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of Saturne, by som constellacioun,</B><BR>
1089 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Hath yeven us this, although we hadde it sworn;</B><BR>
1090 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>So stood the hevene whan that we were born.</B><BR>
1091 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>We moste endure it; this is the short and playn."</B><BR>
1092 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This Palamon answerde and seyde agayn,</B><BR>
1093 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Cosyn, for sothe, of this opinioun</B><BR>
1094 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Thow hast a veyn ymaginacioun.</B><BR>
1095 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This prison caused me nat for to crye,</B><BR>
1096 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But I was hurt right now thurghout myn ye</B><BR>
1097 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Into myn herte, that wol my bane be.</B><BR>
1098 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>The fairnesse of that lady that I see</B><BR>
1099 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yond in the gardyn romen to and fro</B><BR>
1100 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Is cause of al my criyng and my wo.</B><BR>
1101 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I noot wher she be womman or goddesse,</B><BR>
1102 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>But Venus is it soothly, as I gesse."</B><BR>
1103 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And therwithal on knees doun he fil,</B><BR>
1104 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And seyde, "Venus, if it be thy wil</B><BR>
1105 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Yow in this gardyn thus to transfigure</B><BR>
1106 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Bifore me, sorweful, wrecched creature,</B><BR>
1107 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Out of this prisoun help that we may scapen.</B><BR>
1108 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And if so be my destynee be shapen</B><BR>
1109 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>By eterne word to dyen in prisoun,</B><BR>
1110 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of oure lynage have som compassioun,</B><BR>
1111 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That is so lowe ybroght by tirannye."</B><BR>
1112 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with that word Arcite gan espye</B><BR>
1113 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Wher as this lady romed to and fro,</B><BR>
1114 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with that sighte hir beautee hurte hym so,</B><BR>
1115 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That, if that Palamon was wounded sore,</B><BR>
1116 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Arcite is hurt as muche as he, or moore.</B><BR>
1117 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And with a sigh he seyde pitously,</B><BR>
1118 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"The fresshe beautee sleeth me sodeynly</B><BR>
1119 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Of hire that rometh in the yonder place;</B><BR>
1120 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>And but I have hir mercy and hir grace,</B><BR>
1121 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>That I may seen hire atte leeste weye,</B><BR>
1122 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>I nam but deed; ther nis namoore to seye."</B><BR>
1123 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>This Palamon, whan he tho wordes herde,</B><BR>
1124 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>Dispitously he looked and answerde,</B><BR>
1125 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Wheither seistow this in ernest or in pley?"</B><BR>
1126 &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<B>"Nay," quod Arcite, "in ernest, by my fey!</B><BR>
